British Ministry of Agriculture and Fisheries Revises Plant Import Order Regarding Beetroot 94

The Ministry of Industry orders the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau

Should notify relevant merchants

The Ministry of Industry approved the consultation from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, approving the British Ambassador Jardine's statement that the Minister of Agriculture and Fisheries of the United Kingdom issued the 1935 revised plant import order, which came into effect from February 1, 1936. For beetroot (Sugar beet and mangold beta vuigais Linn) transported from foreign countries, all raw vegetables, whole or in part, except for vegetable seeds, are prohibited from being unloaded in England and Wales without the permission of the Ministry of Agriculture and Fisheries. The Scottish Agriculture Board and the Northern Ireland Department of Agriculture have also issued similar orders, so the same regulations also apply in Scotland and Northern Ireland, etc. After the Ministry of Industry approved the consultation, it has ordered the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau to be notified and also instructed relevant merchants to pay attention.

Imported Cotton Seeds Limited to Shanghai for the Time Being 95

Must be inspected and qualified before import is allowed

The National Economic Commission's Cotton Industry Control Committee believes that in order to improve cotton production in recent years, our country has often purchased cotton seeds from the United States. However, imported seeds sometimes contain dangerous insects and bacteria that our country does not have. If disinfection procedures are not carried out at the time of import, the attached insects and bacteria will inevitably enter the country and spread everywhere, and the harm will be unimaginable. A special letter was sent to the Ministry of Industry, requesting that before the implementation of plant pest and disease inspection by the commodity inspection bureaus in various places, the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau should be responsible for the inspection and disinfection of imported cotton seeds. After receiving the letter, the Ministry of Industry expressed its approval in matters of inspection administration. However, plant pest and disease inspection by inspection bureaus other than Shanghai must wait until preparations are complete before they can be opened. The inspection and disinfection of imported cotton seeds should first be handled by the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau. All imported cotton seeds should be temporarily limited to import through Shanghai and must be inspected and qualified before import is allowed. The bureau has been ordered to comply and contact the Jianghai Customs for handling.

National Products: Methods for Importing into the Dutch East Indies 96

No Difficulties Encountered

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce yesterday received a letter from the Overseas Chinese General Chamber of Commerce in Batavia, reporting on the situation of Chinese goods imported into the Dutch East Indies. The Chamber of Commerce has issued a circular to all relevant industries for their information. The original letter is as follows: According to the minutes of the second annual general meeting of the standing directors of our association on the 6th of this month, one of the matters discussed concerned the Dutch East Indies government. Since implementing restrictions on the import of goods from various countries, the Import Bureau of the Ministry of Economic Affairs has granted special preferential treatment to formally registered import firms importing Chinese goods, allowing them to import additional quantities. However, reports in domestic newspapers state that there are various difficulties in importing national products into the Dutch East Indies, which is not in accordance with the facts. The current situation regarding the transit of national products here can be divided into three categories: 1. National products not subject to restrictions in the Dutch East Indies can be freely imported, the same as before. 2. National products that are subject to restrictions can still obtain additional special import permits, provided they have an official permit and export documentation. 3. National products are subject to the same import taxes as goods from other countries, with no exceptional difficulties. We should send letters to chambers of commerce and industrial associations in various parts of the country to clarify the situation regarding the import of national products here. It was resolved to proceed with this matter and to send a letter to inform you and request that you forward the above information to national product manufacturers in your area to correct any misperceptions and benefit national products.

Those present yesterday included Zhu Qinglan, Chairman of the Relief Affairs Committee and Chairman of the Association's Committee; Wang Zhen, Chairman of the Disaster Relief Fund Custody Committee; Mayor Wu Tiecheng (represented by Li Dachao); Yu Zuoting, Chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce; Wang Xiaolai, Speaker of the Municipal Council; Zhu Shaoping, Deputy Director of the Municipal Gazetteer Office; and more than 70 others, including Cheng Jingsheng, Qu Wenliu, Huang Qinglan, Wen Lanting, Mao Yun, and Xiong Xiling.

Chairman's Report

Around 4:00 PM, leaders from all sectors had gathered, and the tea party began. After refreshments were served, Mr. Zhu Qinglan gave a report, saying: "I am extremely honored that all of you great philanthropists and local leaders have graced us with your presence today. I just returned from Nanjing today. Minister Kong could not attend due to important official duties in Beijing and asked me to apologize to you on his behalf. Last year's floods in various provinces were already mitigated by your efforts, and the lives of the disaster victims were extended to this day through various methods such as emergency relief and winter relief. This is truly not easy. But now spring plowing is critical. Many disaster victims are returning after fleeing, and if we don't rush to save them, all our previous efforts will be in vain. I believe all sectors will not bear to see this happen. However, the economy is sluggish, and raising funds is extremely difficult. At this moment, our Shanghai Relief Association for Flood Disasters in Various Provinces, because Ms. Yao of Suzhou destroyed her home to help those in need and donated all her property to our association, we and our colleagues initiated this Goods Relief Association, following the example of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, soliciting relief funds and giving away "Fortune Fruit" tickets. The significance of this is that, on the one hand, it allows those who donate goods to do good deeds, and on the other hand, it allows those who contribute to the relief funds to do good deeds on their behalf, while also giving each individual a small commemorative gift. Therefore, the task of this association is to solicit goods and solicit relief funds to give away "Fortune Fruit" tickets. The two tasks must be carried out simultaneously. The value of the gifts we have already received has reached 80,000 to 90,000 yuan, but the number of items is still less than 3,000. There are not enough gifts to cover all the tickets. This is why we need all of you to help us a lot. Any kind of thing can be donated as a gift first. As for the matter of giving away tickets, in addition to those who have already taken on the responsibility, there are still 4,000 tickets that we need to rely on all of you here to work hard on. As for the method of solicitation, please give us as much guidance as possible. I am certainly one of them, but I hope that we can all work together to give away all 12,000 tickets so that the disaster victims can receive a final relief, which will bring immeasurable blessings to all of you."

Support from All Sides

After Mr. Zhu's report, Mr. Xiong Xiling expressed his opinion, saying: "In recent years, the disaster situation in the country has been serious, and the people are suffering in water and fire. Fortunately, philanthropists have been running around and appealing on behalf of the disaster victims. Now that spring plowing is about to begin, and with Ms. Yao's donation of her family property, issuing 'Fortune Fruit' tickets to help the disaster victims, we should really work hard to complete this good deed." Then, Qu Wenliu reported, saying: "The number of 'Fortune Fruit' tickets issued this time is 120,000 yuan, of which 80,000 yuan will be used to relieve the disaster victims in Subei. The disaster in Subei occurred later, and the disaster situation is more serious than in other provinces. The disaster relief funds allocated at that time have mostly been distributed, so the funds received for emergency relief and winter relief in Subei were particularly small at that time. This time, it should get more, but because of the large number of disaster victims, this small amount is still a drop in the bucket. Therefore, everyone should work hard to save more lives and create more blessings. Of the 120,000 yuan of 'Fortune Fruit' tickets, 80,000 yuan have already been pledged, and the remaining 40,000 yuan should not be difficult to obtain and can hopefully be fully donated in the near future." Then, Li Dachao expressed his opinion on behalf of Mayor Wu, saying: "Mayor Wu expresses his deep sympathy for the issuance of 'Fortune Fruit' tickets this time and hopes to do his best to promote this matter as soon as possible, and hopes that all of you will also work together."

Yu Baoqing 50 tickets, Xiong Xiling 50 tickets, Zhu Shaoping 20 tickets, Deng Xingwu Zhenji Factory combined 10 tickets, totaling about 80,000 yuan. Therefore, it is expected that the total amount of 120,000 yuan can be fully pledged in the near future."

Municipal Council Announces: Investigation of Errors 100

Japanese Side Demands Re-Election

Regarding the error in counting votes in the recent election of foreign councilors of the Shanghai Municipal Council, the Municipal Council issued the following statement yesterday: "This year's election of councilors of the Municipal Council was conducted in accordance with the established practice for many years as stipulated in Article 18 of the Land Regulations. After the closing of the poll, the supervisors of the election, appointed by the Board of Directors, personally secured the ballot boxes at the training room of the Municipal Council Chamber of Commerce and the Hongkou Police Station, and brought them to the meeting room of the Board of Directors of the Municipal Council. Then, the two vote counters appointed by the Board of Directors personally opened them and inspected the ballots obtained. At that time, after the vote counters counted the votes, they reported that a total of 2,482 election ballots and 13 invalid ballots had been obtained, and announced the names of the nine candidates with the most votes. At that time, the vote counters believed that the number of votes counted was accurate, and the list of elected persons was signed by the vote counters and announced by order of the Director-General of the Municipal Council. Afterwards, the election ballots that had been counted were immediately destroyed in accordance with the usual practice to prevent the leakage of the confidentiality of the vote. At this time, the ballot boxes were deemed to be empty and were locked in the Director-General's office. Unexpectedly, the next morning, it was discovered that some election ballots were left in the ballot box sent by the Hongkou Police Station. These election ballots, due to an unexplained error, were left in the box and were not counted. After this matter was discovered, the ballot box was properly kept in custody to await the arrival of the vote counters for a recount. After the vote counters re-inspected the ballots, a total of 323 election ballots were obtained, of which six were invalid. The numbers for the next day were immediately revised, and a new report was issued, signed by the vote counters, and the names of the nine candidates with the most votes were announced."

The Japanese-language Shanghai Nichinichi Shimbun Evening Edition published yesterday stated that the international election battle had come to an end, and as a result, Japan had suffered a defeat. However, the Japanese Election Committee had doubts about the number of votes received and unanimously advocated for clarification. Today, Chairman Lin, along with the head of the Japanese Residents' Association and others, visited Mr. Fessenden and Secretary Johnson of the Municipal Council to question why the number of votes received by the Japanese side was so small, suspecting there were omissions. Mr. Fessenden replied that on the first day of the election, 323 votes from the Hongkou voting station were placed in the machine when they were sent to the office and were forgotten to be counted, so the actual number of votes did not match. Thereupon, Chairman Lin, considering the matter to be bizarre, visited Consul-General Ishii at the Consulate-General for the sake of investigation, and discussed emergency countermeasures with the candidates. At the same time, the attitude of the Japanese community suddenly hardened, because such a scandalous election must be investigated, and it is questionable whether it is fair to open the 323 votes in accordance with the statutory conditions. From the perspective of rectifying the election, the election should be corrected, because the Japanese side cast 2,808 votes, but only 2,483 votes were announced, and it is feared that the number is not even this high. It is argued that the election should be re-held in accordance with the Land Regulations. Mr. Fessenden said that the 323 votes were burned on the spot and could not be checked. If the Japanese side wants to re-hold the election, they can only comply.

Consul-General Xu Nianceng, Stationed in Hanoi, Vietnam: Speaks Freely About the Establishment of the Consulate 103

There Are Approximately 600,000 Overseas Chinese in Vietnam; Mr. Xu Met with Gu Weijun Yesterday Morning to Report on Everything

Mr. Xu Nianceng, the Consul-General stationed in Hanoi, returned to China from his post a few days ago, passed through Shanghai, and went to Beijing to meet with Foreign Minister Zhang to report on the establishment of the consulate. After finishing his business, he returned to Shanghai by car at 7:00 AM yesterday morning. After getting off the car, he went to his hotel to rest. Then, at around 9:00 AM, he drove to the private residence of Ambassador to France Gu Weijun to report on the situation in his area of responsibility, and only left after talking for more than an hour. A reporter from the Xinxin News Agency interviewed Mr. Xu at his hotel yesterday and learned a great deal about the establishment of the consulate in Hanoi and the lives of Overseas Chinese in Vietnam. The details of his conversation are recorded below:

Establishment of the Consulate

According to Mr. Xu, there are a large number of Overseas Chinese in Vietnam. In order to promote Sino-Vietnamese commerce and protect the interests of Overseas Chinese, the government has long considered setting up consulates in Vietnam. The revision of the Sino-French-Vietnamese Treaty was delayed and not agreed upon, so it could not be realized earlier. It was not until May of last year that the Sino-French-Vietnamese Treaty was officially signed and promulgated. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs then decided to open a consulate-general in Hanoi, Vietnam, and a consulate in Saigon. I was ordered to be the first Consul-General stationed in Hanoi, and immediately returned to China from Russia. After receiving instructions from the Ministry, I went to Hanoi and arrived at the end of November last year. After everything was prepared, the consulate was officially opened on December 18th.

Current Situation of Overseas Chinese

The entire territory of Vietnam is divided into five parts: Cochinchina, Annam, Tonkin, Cambodia, and Laos. Tonkin occupies an important position in politics and commerce because it is located in the center of Vietnam and is very close to our country's border. There are more than 600,000 Overseas Chinese in Vietnam, mostly from Guangdong. Among them, more than 200,000 live in Cochinchina, and the rest are scattered in various parts of Annam, Tonkin, and Cambodia. In terms of the occupations of Overseas Chinese in Vietnam, there are many who work as coolies, but there are also many who occupy important positions in commerce. In addition, the scope of the businesses operated by Overseas Chinese in Vietnam is vast and far beyond the reach of local people. Therefore, the prosperity or decline of their businesses is closely related to Vietnamese commerce. It can be imagined how important the position of Overseas Chinese in Vietnam is.

Returning to Post Within a Week

The Vietnamese government authorities treat Overseas Chinese in Vietnam fairly well, so Overseas Chinese can live and work in Vietnam in peace. Now that the consulate has just been established, I have been ordered to be stationed in Vietnam and will naturally follow the government's will and work hard to promote the improvement of relations between the two countries. I will do my best to protect the legitimate interests of Overseas Chinese. As for the business situation of Overseas Chinese in Vietnam, in recent years, due to the impact of the world's economic downturn, there has been a downward trend. However, this situation is prevalent in countries around the world, not just Vietnam, etc. Mr. Xu's return to China this time was to go to Guangdong for negotiations and took the opportunity to pass through Hong Kong to Shanghai and then to Beijing to meet with Foreign Minister Zhang to report on the establishment of the consulate. Now that his business is completed, he plans to return to his ancestral home in Wuxi after bidding farewell to Ambassador Gu before he leaves the country. He is scheduled to leave Shanghai within a week to return to his post.

Supreme Court New Precedent of Mistaken Investment 108

Not Liable for Partnership Responsibility

Since the passing of Huang Chu'er, the various businesses he operated have also successively collapsed, resulting in numerous lawsuits. Several years have passed, yet the repercussions remain unresolved. The Gongfa Company, being one of Huang's key ventures, is no exception. Its debts amount to over three million yuan. Although creditors pursued the outstanding payments and the court executed auctions for compensation, the remaining amount was still eight-tenths of the total debt. Last year, a group of Gongfa's creditors, including Xu Peiyuan, noticed the names of Huayang Pharmacy and others listed in the company's shareholder register. They filed a lawsuit in the Shanghai Second Special District Local Court to confirm partnership. The first instance court ruled in favor of Xu and the others. Huayang Pharmacy, feeling unjustly implicated, hired three lawyers, Li Guozhen, Lü Shifang, and Li Yujun, to file an appeal to the High Court Third Branch. Consequently, the original judgment was overturned, and Xu's claims in the first instance were rejected. Xu Peiyuan and the others, dissatisfied, appealed to the Supreme Court. Now, having reviewed the Supreme Court's Civil Judgment No. 2177 of the 24th year, the court rejected Xu's appeal, stating that "Huayang Pharmacy invested in Gongfa Company mistakenly believing it to be a joint-stock limited company, as determined by the original trial court. Therefore, they cannot be held liable for Gongfa Company's debts as partners." Since the implementation of the New Civil Code, the courts have often ordered joint and several liability for debts incurred by companies claiming to be joint-stock limited companies but not properly registered, regardless of the investor's intentions. This has been not only unfair but also led to financial ruin for some. With this precedent now established, it can be cited for support, thus preventing further unexpected losses.

Summer Ripple's Eastern Voyage Encountered Twists and Turns 109

Mr. Xia Li of Nanhui, after being recommended by Mr. Wang Yiting following Ambassador Xu's order to visit Japan, intended to travel east with them. Unexpectedly, someone made anonymous accusations. After investigation, none of the names listed in the letter existed. Nanhui's various organizations issued a joint statement, asserting that Mr. Xia was enthusiastic about public welfare, always diligent and prudent, and never engaged in the conduct described in the letter, to rectify the situation. County Magistrate Yuan also sent a letter to Mr. Wang, requesting him to convey Mr. Xia's character to Ambassador Xu. Mr. Xia disregarded this kind of senseless attack. Currently, due to other matters requiring organization, the date of Mr. Xia's departure remains uncertain.

Branches Supplying Goods to Headquarters: No Stamp Tax Required on Allocation Lists 110

Yesterday, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce replied to the Tongchang Car Company's Branch Management Department regarding stamp tax issues, stating that it received your letter of February 4th inquiring about the use of stamp tax. Now, the reply is as follows: Regarding the allocation lists used by branches to obtain goods from headquarters, if the relationship between the branch and the headquarters is not as described in the Ministry of Finance's Tax Ruling No. 7213, where "although the names are the same, the capital and operations are entirely independent," then according to Article 3, Clause 8 of the Stamp Tax Law, these allocation lists are internal audit documents and do not require stamp tax. Furthermore, Ministry of Finance's Tax Ruling No. 7137 also states that the allocation lists used by branch factories to report required materials to headquarters are exempt from stamp tax according to Article 3, Clause 8 of the Stamp Tax Law. This can be consulted for exemption. When branches remit funds to headquarters, the drafts issued by the remitter to the entrusted payer should be taxed according to Rate Table Clause 4. However, the remittance stubs used for internal bookkeeping are also exempt from stamp tax according to Article 3, Clause 8 of the Stamp Tax Law.

Fudan University: Seven Communists Arrested Yesterday and the Day Before 111

A small number of Communists incited students to form vigilante groups to prohibit and obstruct, shooting and wounding the police captain and two policemen from outside the school.

Taxpayers' Association Sends Letter to Municipal Council Correcting the Behavior of the Electricity Company 112

Zhong Chunjie Was Forced to Sign, Requesting the Municipal Council to Provide Protection

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Public Settlement sent a letter to the Municipal Council yesterday, stating that, according to a letter from Zhong Chunjie Barber Shop at 799 Huade Road, on the morning of March 24th, the Shanghai Electric Power Company ordered people to invite me to the company for a discussion. I went to the office on Feilun Road before 2:00 PM that afternoon. There were two Westerners and a Chinese employee named Zhu at the scene. They said that the fire wire of my shop would be cut off. If I couldn't afford the fine, I could pay half to settle the matter, and ordered me to sign immediately on a paper slip written by a certain Wang from the company. While someone was reading the contents of the slip to me, there were sentences such as admitting to privately changing the lead seal. Although I do not understand either Chinese or Western languages, I refused to sign. Mr. Zai from the company then replaced it with another slip for me to sign, but did not read out the sentences, only saying that if I didn't sign, they would restrict my freedom of movement and send someone to cut off the fire wire at my shop, making it impossible for me to do business. At the same time, a Westerner raised his fist as if to strike. Fearing physical abuse and the inability to do business, I was forced to sign and leave. At that time, they declared that by the morning of tomorrow (March 25th), I must pay 47 silver dollars, otherwise they would still cut off the wire and I must not report to the Chinese Taxpayers' Association or publish it in the newspaper. I was subjected to this forced coercion and have no way to appeal, so I can only report the truth. I hope your association will quickly forward a letter to the Municipal Council to rectify the illegal actions of the company impartially. Furthermore, because I do not know either Chinese or Western languages, I do not know what the contents of all the above-mentioned sentences are. The document I was forced to sign under duress is completely invalid, I hereby declare." Upon investigation, legally exercising rights is the attitude that people under the rule of law should have. Even if there is an occasional emotional impulse and lack of control, one should admit mistakes in the face of the law when reason is restored. This is the great spirit of the Anglo-Saxon people and the maxim of the ancient Chinese philosophers, "do not hesitate to correct mistakes." Now, the electric power company has not only lost the spirit of the rule of law, but also tries to cover up its mistakes and even bully the weak, intending to interfere with freedom, threatening to cut off wires, and forcing signatures afterwards. Under the supervision of an impartial authority based on the rule of law, the company has engaged in such constant illegal behavior, which is extremely shameful. Accordingly, we request that your bureau severely correct the illegal behaviors of the Shanghai Electric Power Company in self-reporting, self-adjudicating, and self-executing, and stop all bullying actions in order to protect the legal rights and interests of taxpayers. Respectfully addressed to the Director-General of the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Settlement.

Various Public Organizations Hold a Banquet 118

Over 100 Representatives from Various Organizations Attended

Wang Xiaolai, Yang Weiyu, and others all gave speeches

Mr. Lin Aimin, the former manager of the Singapore Sin Chew Jit Poh, returned to China to serve at the invitation of various parties in the country and took the opportunity to inspect the Beijing-Shanghai area. The various public organizations in the city held a banquet at the YMCA last night at 7:00 PM to welcome him. Over 100 representatives and individuals from various public organizations attended. The details of the event are described below.

Participating Representatives

Representatives from public organizations included Zhu Bowen of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, Ren Jinping of the Local Association, Ma Yinliang of Shen Bao, Lu Ganchen of the YMCA, Yang Weiyu of the China Vocational Education Society, Zhang Yuliang of the China Aviation Association, Xie Nanguang of the Fujian Association, Zhu Shaoping of the Chinese Global Student Association, Chen Zongshan of the China-South Cultural Association, Su Yaozhen of the New Yongding Construction Association, and Li Gongpu of the Liangcai Library. Individuals included Wang Xiaolai, Pan Gongzhan, Ma Chonggan, Sun Daosun, Liu Shimu, and Ma Gongyu, totaling over 100 people.

Chairman's Speech

First, Chairman Wang Xiaolai delivered a welcoming speech on behalf of the entire group, stating that Mr. Lin has devoted himself to the newspaper industry in Southeast Asia with great success, making a significant contribution to strengthening the national consciousness of overseas Chinese. His return to the country to serve, with his past experience and achievements, will undoubtedly make many contributions and add a unique color to the domestic press. I hope that Mr. Lin will maintain his enthusiasm for caring for the motherland, which he had when serving in Southeast Asia, and will not forget the overseas Chinese in order to make contributions to the country and the nation. On behalf of the entire group, I raise my glass to wish Mr. Lin a bright future and good health.

Mr. Lin's Reply

Mr. Lin then rose to reply, stating that he was extremely grateful for the welcome banquet hosted by the various public organizations and gentlemen tonight. I have lived in Southeast Asia for over ten years, and only recently returned from overseas. I would like to take this opportunity to briefly report on the situation of overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia. Over a hundred years ago, Southeast Asia was still a desolate land. Our overseas Chinese ancestors first ventured there to do business, enduring countless hardships before achieving today's prosperity. However, in recent years, the status of overseas Chinese has been greatly reduced. The global economic downturn is one reason, but the political environment of the location, which places restrictions on overseas Chinese everywhere, is the biggest reason. Currently, the Japanese are using their superior political and economic power to squeeze out overseas Chinese in all aspects. In the future, if the overseas Chinese themselves do not have a sound organization, they will inevitably find it difficult to resist. I sincerely hope that our government and farsighted compatriots will provide guidance and assistance so that our overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia can restore their past glory.

Founding a New Newspaper

Mr. Lin also reported on his future work. He stated that I and various friends have decided to create an ideal newspaper in South China, based on the principle of high quality, small quantity, and high sales, in order to connect the voices of China and Southeast Asia. Preparations have already begun, and it will be named the "Dahua Daily." It will be launched in three or four months. In addition, Mr. Ma Xiangbo advocated organizing a Southeast Asian Research Society to publish yearbooks and other publications on Southeast Asian issues. I have always been committed to cultural undertakings, so I have accepted the invitation and started preparations. This trip to Shanghai, in addition to inspection, is also to set up the headquarters in Shanghai.

Mr. Yang's Speech

Yang Weiyu, the representative of the Vocational Education Society, then gave a speech, stating that welcoming Mr. Lin has two more meanings. First, domestic compatriots have always admired overseas Chinese compatriots, and the contributions of overseas Chinese to the motherland have always been great. Dr. Sun Yat-sen's revolution and the January 28th Anti-Japanese War received more support from overseas Chinese in terms of material and spirit than from the country. Overseas Chinese who provide material assistance are worthy of praise, but without cultural figures like Mr. Lin to advocate, how could this be achieved? Secondly, foreigners have always looked down on our country, slandering it as a culturally backward country. In their impressions, they believe that Chinese people only know how to do business and make money. With overseas Chinese cultural figures like Mr. Lin to promote, foreigners will have a new understanding of us, and understand the great personality and strength of our people, bringing honor and dignity to the country. The national achievements are much greater than those who only provide material assistance to the motherland. Subsequently, Li Chonghou, a professor at the College of Law and Political Science, and others gave speeches in succession. The event ended happily at about 9:00 PM.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Yangtze River Ships Jointly Operate with Nanxun Railway 119

Orders Have Been Issued Yesterday

Effective April 1st

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's combined water-land transport only involves the mutual connection of cargo with various railways. However, the passenger transport between trains and ships has not been realized due to various factors such as time and schedules. Since Cai Zengji took office, in addition to reorganizing the internal and external personnel of the bureau and reforming the systems of wharves and warehouses, he has also negotiated with the Nanxun Railway to launch a combined passenger transport service for the Nanxun Railway and Yangtze River ships. Both parties have reached an agreement, and the method will be temporarily based on the first passenger train departing from Nanchang to Jiujiang. Passengers from all stations along the Qianjiang River from Nanchang to Jiujiang who wish to go to Anqing, Wuhu, Nanjing, Zhenjiang, and Shanghai can connect with the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's downriver ships. Passengers do not have to wait for ships when they arrive at Xun, wasting time. The Nanxun Railway and the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company have agreed that every ship departing from Hankou to Shanghai will not leave the Xun port wharf until 1:00 PM after arriving in Jiujiang, regardless of whether there are connecting passengers. (That is, after the first train from Nanxun arrives in Jiujiang). Yesterday, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, led by Deputy Directors Chen Zhaoji and Zhou Houkun of the Shipping Department and Director Shi Yixuan of the Business Department, issued an order to all Yangtze River ship captains and telegraphed the Nanxun Railway to comply. The combined passenger transport of trains and ships is the first record, which will be implemented on April 1st.

Shanghai-Nanjing Railway and Jiangnan Railway to Operate Combined Passenger Transport 120

Effective April 1st

Pilot Program for One Month

The Shanghai-Nanjing Railway and the Jiangnan Railway are connected at Yaohuamen Station to operate combined passenger transport. After both parties worked together to complete the construction of the connecting tracks and bridges, it was decided to implement it on April 1st. The existing Shanghai-Nanjing Railway's No. 4 upbound express train and No. 21 downbound express train will be used for the joint operation. Each party will provide one first-class car, one second-class car, one third-class car, and one baggage car. As the stopping time at the station must be at least seven minutes to complete the shunting work, the total travel time of the train will be extended by ten minutes. At the request of the Jiangnan Railway, the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway will also add stops to the No. 3, No. 6, and No. 22 trains at Yaohuamen Station for the convenience of connecting passengers getting on and off, and will slightly change the departure times of each train. A pilot program will be implemented for one month first.

Fire in Zhabei Zhonghua Xin Road Destroys Over 100 Thatched Houses 124

Disaster Victims Supporting the Old and Carrying the Young

The cries were heartbreaking

Yesterday morning at around 5:00 AM, a fire suddenly broke out in the thatched shacks near Zhonghua Xin Road in Zhabei Gonghe Xin Road. Because the thatched shacks were entirely made of grass, once they caught fire, they spread rapidly and were unstoppable. Girl Picks Up a Bomb, Mother and Daughter Are Injured by the Explosion 125

Yesterday morning at around 10:30 AM, Chen Xiaoma, a seven-year-old girl from the Chen Jinren family, who are immigrants from Jiangbei and live in a nameless thatched house near East Sports Association Road in Jiangwan, was scavenging nearby when she found a bomb in the bushes. At the time, Xiaoma did not know what it was, thinking it was a toy, and happily brought it home to show her mother, Chen Dong, who was 43 years old. However, Chen Dong also did not recognize it, thinking it was scrap metal. At that time, she was cooking rice, and she put the bomb into the fire. Before long, the bomb exploded, with a loud bang and flying shrapnel, injuring Chen Dong's left foot. Xiaoma's face and limbs were also seriously injured. Mother and daughter were immediately covered in blood and fell to the ground. Fortunately, the nearby police officers heard the alarm and rushed to the scene, and took the mother and daughter to the hospital for treatment. Their condition is critical.

Chen Xuezhen is she a mute?

Sent to Forensic Institute for Further Examination

Chen Hongfu, a farmer from Yanjiachengjiao, Gaoqiao, Pudong, and originally from Chongming, was beaten and had two ribs broken on the night of the twenty-sixth day of the tenth month of the lunar calendar last year, resulting in his death. He also repeatedly ordered Chen Qiufu, the deceased's brother, to bring the girl Chen Xuezhen for questioning. The day before yesterday afternoon, presiding judge Cai Dingcheng opened the court for renewed trial. The details of the questioning have already been reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now learned that Judge Cai, considering the significant discrepancies in this case, summoned Chen Xuezhen for questioning. Surprisingly, Xuezhen remained silent throughout. When questioned, eight-year-old boy Chen Jinxiang stated that Xuezhen called him "second brother," leading to the deduction that Xuezhen was clearly not a mute. Therefore, it was ordered that Xuezhen be temporarily handed over to her mother, Chen Huang, to be taken to the detention center for care. Yesterday afternoon, a letter was sent to the police to bring Chen Qiufu, the deceased's brother, along with Chen Xuezhen, to the Zhenru Forensic Institute to examine the truth behind Chen Xuezhen's unwillingness to speak, and perhaps there are other hidden circumstances, and will be verified again.

had a child

who has since died. However, this scandalous affair was discovered by Ji A'da in prison. Ji became extremely angry, believing that his imprisonment was actually a malicious setup by Sun Genan. and Sun also learned about the situation from his colleagues and had a sense of caution. Therefore, in addition to severing ties with Ji's wife Tao, he was also careful to guard against it. fled in fear

attempted murder

according to Article 271, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law. The defendant also came to demand money and make trouble from time to time. If he didn't deal with it, he would kill me. grabbed his hands

and the gun fell on the bed. The shop assistants then called the police to arrest him. Xu Jinlong and Shen Huikang, the witnesses, also testified that they saw the defendant arrive with a gun. When questioned, Ji A'da stated that after I was arrested for the case, I was released on January 15th last year, and Sun seduced my wife at this time. On the 19th of this month, because my wife was about to give birth, I negotiated with Sun. Sun voluntarily subsidized 20 yuan, telling me to come to the store at 10 AM yesterday to collect the money. Therefore, I

went on time

but was arrested by the police. The gun was not mine, or Sun used his old tricks to frame me. Sun is cunning by nature, and everyone in the industry knows this, which can be investigated. Zhu Yanqing Brothers Sued Again by Younger Sister 130

Inheritance Disputes Lead to Endless Litigation

Discovery of False and Fraudulent Deeds

After the death of Zhu Baoyuan, the owner of Zhenhe Tea Shop from Haining, all his inheritance was managed by his adopted sons, Yanqing and Shunqing. Zhu Baoyuan's married daughters, Zhu Jun and Zhu Meizhen, etc., had repeatedly litigated with their two brothers in the First Special District Court over the division of the inheritance, which was later settled with each receiving 80,000 yuan. However, Zhu Baoyuan's youngest daughter, Zhu Lizhen, also sued her brother Yanqing in the Haining County Court for forging a will. After investigation by the prosecutor, a decision was made not to prosecute. Subsequently, after mediation, she received property worth 80,000 yuan, the same as Zhu Jun and others. This was on September 8th of last year. However, Lizhen was only seventeen years old at the time, so in December of the same year, a custody deed was signed, stating that all property due to Lizhen would be temporarily kept by her two brothers until Lizhen came of age. Now, Zhu Lizhen, on the grounds that her brothers did not fulfill the deed, transfer the real estate, and obtained a letter from He Chongnan, discovered that the deed signed at the time was based on falsehood and fraud. Therefore, she hired lawyer Gao Danhua to file a complaint with the First Special District Court, suing Zhu Yanqing and Zhu Shunqing, requesting the cancellation of the signed property division deed. Yesterday, presiding judge Zhang Yuhai of the First Special District Court opened the Fourth Civil Court for questioning. The two defendants hired lawyers Zhang Zhengxue and Jiang Yiping for defense. First, lawyer Gao explained the process and presented He Chongnan's letter as evidence. Then, the defendant's lawyers argued that there was no so-called falsehood or fraud when the deed was signed. The plaintiff had previously been seduced and fell in love with a partner of the Zhenhe Tea Shop opened by the defendant. The plaintiff intended to marry him, but the defendant refused. The partner then instigated the plaintiff to sue for forging a will in the Haining Court, which resulted in no prosecution. After the settlement was reached, due to the restrictions of the custody deed, the plaintiff could not dispose of the property, hence today's lawsuit. Therefore, they requested that the plaintiff's lawsuit be rejected. Judge Zhang, considering that the case still required investigation, ordered an adjournment for further questioning and ordered both parties to appear in court in person.

Xu Shixun and Yang Shouzhang, the nephew of the factory owner Yang Xinan (also known as Yang Jifang), seized more than 90 boxes of pills and liquids, and seven books of accounts from Puda and the Ruixin Pharmaceutical Factory formerly opened on North Henan Road, and sent them to the Special Court. Xu and Yang were ordered to be detained. The details have been recorded in yesterday's newspaper. It is now learned that the seized drugs include 6 boxes of "Dwarf Gourd Pills," which have been verified by the Shanghai Municipal Council Health Department to contain 53% morphine, 12 boxes of "Annao Bupills,"

containing morphine

0.77%, 62 boxes of "Dwarf Gourd Extract," containing 31% morphine, and 18 boxes of "Annao Sleeve Juice," the toxic ingredients contained in them are considerable. In May last year, the factory's production and sale of the above-mentioned drugs were searched by the police, and the drug seller Liu was sentenced to imprisonment. strict investigation

Jiangda Steamer Rescues Drowning Boatman at Huangshiji 134

Two Civilian Boats Capsized by Huge Waves

Four People Rescued, One Frozen to Death

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Yangtze River steamer Jiangda, was sailing from Hankou to Shanghai. On the way, it encountered a civilian boat capsized by wind and waves. It rescued four people and one was frozen to death. Yesterday, the ship arrived in Shanghai and reported to the Shipping Administration Bureau. The details are as follows:

Civilian Boats Encounter Wind

The Jiangda steamer was sailing downstream near Huangshiji in Jiujiang when it encountered two civilian boats, which were traveling together with intertwined ropes, fully loaded with firewood and other items, traveling upstream. It was 3 PM at that time, and the wind and waves were very strong that day. One of the two boats was overturned by the wind and waves, and the other boat intertwined with it was dragged down and sunk. As a result, the two civilian boats capsized one after another, and all the boatmen fell into the water.

Jiangda Helps Rescue

After the boatmen of the two civilian boats fell into the water, they shouted for help in the water. At this time, the Jiangda steamer happened to pass by the area and heard the shouts. The ship immediately stopped and quickly released a sampan into the river for rescue. After various difficulties, all five boatmen who fell into the water were completely rescued. One of them had been in the water for a long time due to the cold weather and had already frozen to death when he was rescued. The other four were rescued.

Collecting Money for Relief

After the four rescued people were asked by the captain of the Jiangda steamer, they learned that the civilian boats were loaded with firewood from Anqing to the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. Unfortunately, they encountered wind in the middle of the journey, and both boats capsized. Fortunately, they were rescued by the noble ship, but all their money, clothes, and belongings had been lost. How could they return to Anhui? The captain had a compassionate intention. In addition to providing them with clothes and food, he also solicited donations from various crew members and passengers on the ship, totaling seventy or eighty yuan, which was handed over to the four boatmen and sent to Jiujiang. The boatmen were instructed to disembark, and the donated money was used as travel expenses for their return to Anhui.

Almost Ran Aground

When Jiangda stopped to assist in the rescue, the area happened to be a shoal. After the civilian boats capsized, the river surface was also covered with the reeds they were carrying. Some of them were already rolled into the engine leaves of the Jiangda steamer. As a result, the movement of the ship lost its flexibility. Fortunately, the captain and chief engineer found a way to avoid retreating and removed the reeds from the propeller, which turned the danger into safety and prevented the ship from running aground. Yesterday, when Jiangda arrived in Shanghai, the captain had reported the matter to the General Bureau and the Shipping Administration Bureau.

Wang Shulou's Trial Record of the Major Robbery Case at the Post Office 135

Wang Directly Admits Going to Robbery for the Booty

Jih Wears Monk's Robes and Still Tries to Evade

The major robbery and bloody case at the North Sichuan Road Postal Administration occurred on September 9th last year. Subsequently, the police arrested a group of men and women from Jiangbei, including Jih Rentang (also known as Wukong Monk), and sent them to the First Special District Court. Jih Rentang was sentenced to life imprisonment, Wang Chen and Jih Chen were sentenced to three years each, and Qiu Guobin was sentenced to two years and six months. Jih Rentang was dissatisfied with the sentence and appealed to the Second High Court, awaiting sentencing. The leader of the case, Wang Shulou (also known as Chen Yuren) from Funing, was still at large. On the afternoon of the 17th of this month, at 1 PM, Chinese detective Huang Yufu and detective Pan Yunlong of the Yulin Road police station learned that he had been hiding at No. 7 Zhifu Road recently. They cooperated with Western detectives to secretly go to the address and arrest him. He was sent to the court for questioning and detention. The details have been recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Jiang Shuzi came to the Third Criminal Court to conduct a trial. Shanghai Municipal Council lawyer Zhang Shizhu claimed that the two gangs were behind the robbery of the post office. One gang was headed by Zhang Lao Jiao, and the other gang was headed by the main offender Jih Rentang. He belonged to Zhang Lao Si's gang. They discussed the matter before the robbery, and the firearms were borrowed from a certain place in Jiangbei. Zhang Lao Si accompanied him to the post office to see the location. Then, they drank tea at the tiger stove on Linping Road, Zhabei. They had a car ready for the robbery, with a Li Jiao as the driver. Jih Rentang also went. At that time, they were carrying Mauser pistols and handguns. At about 9 AM, they saw the security guard and the old quartermaster who was carrying the banknotes in a hemp bag coming down from the building. The gang opened fire and robbed them. After the incident, they divided the spoils in a Jiangbei guild hall in a remote area of Qimei Road. He received 12,000 yuan. Later, he lived with a Jiangxi woman named A'xiang and fled to Nanchang. He came to Shanghai recently and was arrested. Now, Jih Rentang, Qiu Guobin, Wang Chen, and Jih Chen have been determined to be accomplices and have testified in the case. He asked for strict punishment according to law. Judge Jiang ordered the Wang criminal to confront the determined accomplices separately. Wang Chen said that at that time, he lived at No. 1227, Siwen Lane, Dongxinqiao. Wang Shulou and Jih Rentang had come to the place several times. Jih Chen said that he had also seen the defendant and Jih Rentang come to Wang Chen's place to discuss the matter. Qiu Guobin initially said that he did not know the Wang criminal. The court asked him to tell the truth, and he said that he had seen him at Wang Chen's place. Jih Rentang, wearing a monk's robe, said that he did not know the defendant at all, hoping to reduce his crime in the appeal. He testified cunningly. When questioned, Wang Shulou confessed without denying. He said that he had received 9,000 yuan, and his lover A'xiang had taken 3,000 yuan, which he had spent. At that time, he had divided the spoils in the Jiangbei guild hall. Zhang Lao Jiao had received 230,000 yuan, and Jih Monk had received 34,000 yuan. Two groups went to the post office to rob, and there were more than a dozen accomplices. Judge Jiang appointed lawyer Lin Yingqing to provide free legal assistance to the defendant, and then ordered Wang Shulou to be returned to prison for a scheduled sentencing. It was noon when the court adjourned.

Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau Notifies Opium Smokers to Exchange Second-Term Smoking Cessation Permits 136

From April 1st to the End of May. Failure to Register Within the Deadline Will Result in Permit Cancellation.

The Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau will process the exchange of second-term smoking cessation permits, starting from April 1st and ending on May 31st. Failure to register within the deadline will result in the cancellation of the first-term permits. The details are listed below.

The case of exchanging permits for the second term on April 1st. In accordance with Article 9 of the Regulations on Strictly Enforcing Smoking Cessation and Suppressing Opium Users, the limited-term smoking cessation permits must be exchanged every six months. The registration of opium smokers in this city began in July 1935 and ended in December. The limited-term smoking cessation permits issued in the first term at the end of December are about to expire and must be exchanged to comply with the law. With the approval of the Municipal Government, the bureau will begin the exchange registration on April 1st. All opium smokers who have registered and obtained permits at the bureau and its various sub-bureaus must go to the sub-bureaus and teams in their respective areas to register for the permit exchange procedures starting on April 1st. Those who do not register by May 31st will have their old permits invalidated. Hereafter, smoking opium without a permit will be considered private smoking without a permit and will be sent to military tribunals for prosecution and punishment according to law. Do not delay and bring trouble upon yourselves. As for the first-term smoking cessation permits, a small number of opium smokers either registered under false names or borrowed the addresses of others, which aroused the suspicion of the investigators, who considered them to be using counterfeit permits and arrested them. Although they were released after verification, they were subjected to a short period of detention. Although this was their own fault, their situation is somewhat understandable. In order to make the registration more accurate, opium smokers are allowed to apply for changes if the names, occupations, ages, and addresses they previously reported do not match those listed in their household registrations. After the police have verified the facts, the changes will be made. In addition to the notice, the following are the instructions for exchanging smoking cessation permits. Please abide by them and do not violate them. This is a special notice.

Instructions for Exchanging Limited-Term Permits

The registration date for the second-term permit exchange is from April 1st to May 31st of this year. Failure to register within the deadline will result in the invalidation of the first-term permit. The bureau has obtained approval to not increase the burden on opium smokers. The fee for exchanging ordinary limited-term smoking cessation permits is still 5 yuan, and the fee for exchanging limited-term smoking cessation permits for the poor is still 6 jiao. Opium smokers must submit their first-term permits and second-term permit fees to the bureaus and teams in their respective areas during the permit exchange registration period to apply for permit exchange registration and report their accurate names, ages, birthplaces, occupations, addresses, and other items. After the bureaus and teams that handle the permit exchange have verified and registered the information, they will issue temporary receipts for safekeeping and temporary use. Opium smokers who have registered for the permit exchange must bring their temporary receipts to the bureau or team where they registered to exchange for the official second-term permits within half a month after registration. Opium smokers who hold first-term registration receipts must go to the bureau or team where they originally registered to exchange for the first-term permits and then apply for permit exchange registration in accordance with the procedures.

Artist Gao Jianfu Arrives in Shanghai 138

Artist Gao Jianfu arrived in Shanghai from Guangdong yesterday. Those who welcomed him at the pier included Jian Youwen, Li Minwei, He Yongren, Wu Gonghu, Lu Danlin, and others. Gao devoted himself to art and the national revolution in his early years. He served as the chairman of the Tongmenghui and the commander-in-chief of the Revolutionary Allied Forces in 1911. Since the founding of the Republic of China, he has retreated to devote himself to the art movement. He went to various countries to promote Chinese painting. Last year, he held a solo exhibition in Beijing, which caused a sensation. Central University specially hired him as a professor, but he was unable to take the position due to illness. Recently, Central University repeatedly urged him, so Gao came to Shanghai with his illness to go to Beijing. The Shanghai literary and art community will hold a grand welcome.

Sun Jinshui Punished for Embezzlement 139

Family Still Unaware

Sun Jinshui, a 22-year-old native of Shaoxing, resides in the Houganfang area of Junli, Shaoxing. His father's name is Sun Fengshan. Sun Jinshui has been working as a traveling salesman at the Nanyuan Dananhuo Store, number 38 Laiyi Wharf, for many years. He has generally been diligent and conscientious. However, starting around November of last year, he suddenly changed his ways, spending lavishly. As a result, he embezzled funds from the store, amounting to over 554 yuan. He also pawned a bicycle belonging to the store for 20 yuan in national currency, spending all of it. The store owner eventually discovered this and entrusted lawyer Fang Junjie to report the matter to the Dongjiadu Police Station according to the law. Sun was arrested and transferred to the local court. Judge Wu Zongyu concluded the trial and sentenced him to six months of imprisonment. The store owner's accompanying civil suit was also ruled in his favor, with Sun ordered to pay a total of over 574 yuan in compensation. After the sentence was handed down, Sun, aware of the irrefutable evidence against him, immediately entered prison to serve his term. However, his family, residing far away in Shaoxing, remains unaware of his arrest and imprisonment, or that he requires rescue.

Overview of the Organization of the Shanghai Grain Merchants Guild (Continued) (Nineteenth in the Series on Shanghai Industrial and Commercial Conditions) 150

— Edited by China Credit Bureau

3. Shanghai Rice and Grain Dealers Association: This association was founded in the winter of the sixth year of the Republic of China (1917) by the former Shanghai North and Shanghai South Rice and Grain Dealers Association and a portion of the kebang (merchant group) vendors. The association is located at the intersection of Guangfu Road and Changan Road in Zhabei. Rice and grain dealers are called "maitou" (sellers) in the industry, similar to the brokers who handle the buying and selling of miscellaneous grains and steamed buns. However, its organization is complete, its power is great, and its business is stable, far surpassing the miscellaneous grain brokers who only seek small profits. There are a total of fifty to sixty people in the industry, all operating as individuals, divided into gangs based on the region of the rice and grain producing area: including Changbang (Changshu), Xibang (Wuxi), Xianbang (Jiangyin), Kunbang (Kunshan), Libang (Liyang), Danbang (Danyang), Chengbang (Changzhou), Subang (Suzhou), Nanbang (Songjiang, Wujiang area), Wanbang (specializing in Anhui goods), Jiangbei Gang, and Sanbang, which has little cargo coming. In the past, the Shanghai North Dealers Association had greater power because cargo was concentrated in Zhabei, and rice distributors were mostly in the North. However, distributors in the North mainly specialized in rice distribution, unlike businesses in the South, which mostly used foreign rice as their main commodity. However, in recent years, the rice businesses in the North have declined, and rice wharves have been established in the South, and the power has tended to shift to the South. The dealers are no longer divided into Shanghai North and Shanghai South. Fan Hesheng had the most prestige in the association in the past. After Fan's death, Jiang Shizhi, Zhang Songtao, and others have become slightly well-known. The current chairman of the committee is Zhang Songtao. The association's funds were initially donated by each member, but later a small fee was added to the sale of rice. In addition, there are similar groups, some of which have been merged into the association, and some of which are newly created. Here is a brief description:

I. Changzhao, Nanbang, Beibang and other public offices: Before the establishment of the Rice and Grain Dealers Association, the Changzhao Public Office, Nanbang Public Office, and Beibang Public Office were already established. The Changzhao and Nanbang Public Offices occupy a considerable position in the industry. Other groups of rice merchants stationed in Shanghai, sometimes called public associations or public offices, are also called federations. Its constituent members are nothing more than dealers, mainland rice merchants, vendors, self-purchasing ship owners, carrier ship owners, and those related to the above. Those who were established earlier have been registered, and those who have been organized in recent years have not gone through legal procedures. This is because there may be points of conflict with the registration regulations of the trade association.

II. Shanghai South Rice Transporters and Merchants United Association: This association is temporarily organized and consists of rice shipping households, transporters, and a portion of the dealers. It is often seen in newspapers in the midst of rice price disputes. At that time, it was initiated by the Tonglibang (i.e., Nanbang) vendors and shippers, and then invited other gangs to join, and with the support of powerful people, the power expanded. However, those in the industry who are knowledgeable and afraid of trouble avoid it, because some actions have occurred that have aroused social disgust and criticism. Although it is gradually proceeding on the right track, it has not yet been registered due to internal organizational defects.

III. Shanghai North Rice Transporters and Merchants United Association: The organization of this association is the same as the Shanghai South United Association, and it has not been established for long. It was also promoted by the Shanghai South United Association. Most of the organizers are dealers and few are ship vendors.

4. Shanghai Rice Shop Trade Association: This association has been established for a long time and was reorganized from the Jiagutang Rice Industry Association. Jiagutang was established in the year of Xushen (1908) during the Guangxu period of the former Qing Dynasty. It was first called the public villa and then the public office. In the year of Gengxu (1910) of the Xuantong period, it was renamed the Jiagutang Rice Industry Association. At that time, only 148 North and South counterparts joined the association. After the civil movement broke out in the sixteenth year of the Republic of China (1927), there was also a new organization of rice merchant people in the industry, the Rice Industry Merchant People's Association, which stood opposite Jiagutang. In the eighteenth year of the Republic of China (1929), the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce ordered the merger, and it was reorganized into the Shanghai Rice Shop Trade Association. The association is located on Danfeng Street, Xinkaihe, with branches in both the North and South cities. The current chairman of the committee is Lu Wenshao, and there are about 1,000 members, which is six or seven times more than before. The association occupies an important position in various industry associations in the city, because it has many members and is related to people's food. The Jiagutang of the rice shop industry and the Rengutang of the rice industry have their own organizations and are not mixed. Outsiders regard them as one, but in reality, they are not. The so-called rice shop is a retail store that uses sheng and dou (measuring units); the rice business is a wholesale business, buying and selling in bulk, using hu (another measuring unit), obtaining a brokerage license from the government, directly purchasing goods from cargo owners in various producing areas, adding commissions, and reselling to rice shops. Rice shops cannot wholesale directly from kebangs, etc., and must agree with the distributors and pay a considerable commission before they can implement it. This is the major difference between rice shops and rice businesses. However, among the distributors, there are those who also operate retail sales, and among the shop merchants, there are also those who also operate wholesale sales; because they are all members of the above two trade associations at the same time.

5. Trade Organization of the Flour and Bran Industry

I. Shanghai Flour Mill Trade Association: This association was established during the late Qing Dynasty and was originally named the Shanghai Machinery Flour Company Association. The reason why it had the word "machinery" was to distinguish it from the old-fashioned mills that were still in use at the time. The manufacturers also had the name of a machine-made flour company. In addition to all the factories in Shanghai, the factories in Wuxi were also affiliated with the association. At its peak, there were more than 30 members. However, recently, there are only Fuxin, Fufeng, Huafeng, Shenda, and Maoxin and Jiufeng in Wuxi. The Yutongxiangxin and Erchang factories have long been leased and operated by Fufeng. Huafeng has been closed for a long time and is currently seeking takeover. Since Xinda closed down last year, it has now been leased by Fufeng and operated by Zaoji. Zhonghua also closed down last autumn, and the Xinji (Lida) factory, which Xin Da once rented, has not yet been taken over. Therefore, there are currently only about 20 members in the association. The association is located on Xinkaihe, Minquan Road, and the chairman of the committee is Rong Zongjing. The association once formed a Wheat Office with rice and grain distributors and established branches in the mainland. However, it seems that the association's affairs are currently suspended.

II. Su, Zhe, and Wan Mainland Flour Mill Trade Association: This association, abbreviated as the Mainland Flour Association, was founded in the first year of the Republic of China (1912) and was organized by factories in the mainland of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui provinces. The association is located on Baker Road, and the current chairman of the committee is Cai Jiansan. It is undeniable that the mainland factories' assets and output are not as good as those of the Shanghai factories, and they are scattered in various places and are not easy to contact. Their status is not as important as that of the Shanghai Factory Trade Association, and the association's organization and management are not as sound as those of the Shanghai Association. However, most of the factories in the mainland maintain it. Among the more famous factories, such as Datong Yangtze in Nanjing, Baoxing and Xinfeng in Bengbu, Baoxing in Xuzhou, and Yixin in Yanhu, Hengfeng and other factories in Changzhou, have been reorganized once or several times.

III. Shanghai Flour Exchange Brokers Association: This association is a part of the Flour Exchange organization. The office officially opened on January 11th of the ninth year of the Republic of China (1920). The quota of flour brokers is 55, which cannot be increased or decreased at will. The restrictions on qualifications are very strict, and they must be reported to the Ministry of Industry and approved by the office before they can be changed. The purpose of the Brokers Association is to promote the business of all brokers on the one hand and to assist the development of the entire transaction on the other hand. The president system was initially adopted, but later changed to a committee system. Yang Jinchen and Zhu Jiansheng are the chairman and vice chairman of the association.

The staff of the Shanghai Flour Education Institute formerly organized the Shanghai Flour Exchange Members Association. This is similar to the nature of a trade union, specializing in contacting feelings and mutual assistance and protection, which is different from a business group. Later, internal disputes occurred in the association and it was automatically dissolved.

IV. Shanghai Bran Trade Association: This association was formerly known as the Bran Association. It is not a group of manufacturers and distributors, but is organized by bran brokers who are in the nature of dealers. In the past, when the organization was formed, it was based on individuals and was initiated by more than a dozen people including Shen Chunjiang, Weng Xiaoting, and the late Zai Mingfu. Later, it gradually expanded and changed from individual units to business names. Many soybean, rice, and miscellaneous grain firms that also operated bran joined the association. Flour business names and brokers in the Miscellaneous Grain Flour Exchange also participated. Therefore, its power is quite strong. Moreover, brokers in this industry are different from brokers in other industries. Most of them have abundant assets and operate on a large scale. The internal organization is similar to that of business names. It was just that individuals came forward in the beginning, so they changed their names to business names. Also, due to the different industries, it is divided into two factions: one specializes in Dongyang Zhuang (Japanese goods), and the other specializes in mainland goods; however, most of them operate in both. The address of the head office is in Cotton Yangli, Dou City Street, and the branch office is located in the Shanghai Flour Exchange. The former chairman of the committee, Mr. Shen Chunjiang, passed away this spring, and Weng Xiaoting was elected by the industry to preside over it. (To be continued)

Educational News

Contents of the Special Education Program Drafted by the Ministry of Education 151

Deemed Crucial by President Chiang After Review

The Ministry is Instructed to Formulate Concrete Implementation Measures

(Central News Agency, Nanjing, 25th) To meet the needs of the national crisis, the Ministry of Education solicited opinions from all parties some time ago, and after convening meetings for discussion, it has drafted a special education program and submitted it to President Chiang of the Executive Yuan for review. It is now reported that the program has been reviewed and deemed crucial by President Xie, and the ministry has been instructed to formulate concrete implementation measures. The Ministry of Education is now rushing to draft concrete implementation measures, and the basic goals of the program will be issued before the spring break. The basic goals are to 1. Emphasize physical training, 2. Strengthen spiritual training, 3. Focus on production capacity and special teaching materials in terms of knowledge and skills. The main items of the program are as follows: - Regarding strengthening moral and physical training in schools at all levels, they are: (A) improving all subjects related to physical training, (B) rigorously implementing the integration of education and training, (C) improving and expanding scout training, (D) implementing compulsory physical education, (E) stipulating youth labor service methods, (F) holding special lectures. - Regarding reorganizing the curriculum of schools at all levels and setting up academic and technical subjects, in addition to the revision of the primary and secondary school curriculum, which has been announced, they are: (A) Specialized schools and above should add special academic subjects to their undergraduate programs or conduct research on special academic subjects in research institutes. (B) The Ministry of Education will individually formulate the addition of the aforementioned academic subjects with each school according to the school's equipment and faculty conditions. (C) High schools, normal schools, and senior vocational schools should add special technical subjects within the scope of not hindering basic training and the permissible number of hours per week. The ministry will formulate and issue standards for each province and city to follow and individually set them with each school. - Regarding rigorously implementing mass training, they are: (A) promoting mass schools, (B) improving mass supplementary reading materials, (C) promoting broadcasting education, (D) promoting film education. In addition, the following are also included: - Stepping up the promotion of compulsory education for school-age children. - Expanding production education. - Adjusting the regional distribution of higher education. All have been set by other methods. In general, the purpose of the entire plan is to enrich the content of education at all levels, correct its weaknesses, and focus on practical application, while ensuring that the regular basic training of schools at all levels is not unduly affected.

(Nanjing, 25th) The Military Headquarters organized the Special Education Committee in the 23rd year of the Republic (1934) and established special education offices in Gan, Min, Wan, E, and Yu provinces to handle special education in those provinces.
