School Investigation

Overview of the Shanghai American School (II) 164

— Hu Zuyin

2. A Glimpse of the School Buildings

In the international environment of Shanghai, the buildings of the school are able to express the color of American school architecture. The buildings are surrounded by green lawns, and the interior is mostly luxurious, which can evoke the aesthetic sense of visitors.

Office The office faces Avenue Petain and is the largest building in the school. The first floor houses the offices of various departments, a portion of the elementary school classrooms, and the woodworking classroom. The second floor houses the secondary school classrooms, the auditorium, the library, and the chemistry, physics, and home economics laboratories. Although there are a few classrooms on the third floor, most of them are used as offices for student extracurricular activities, such as the student publishing house, the Girl Scout troop headquarters, the student sports department, and the student self-government association.

Elementary School Building In the northeast corner of the school, there is a building dedicated to young elementary school children. Inside are the kindergarten and first-grade classrooms, and outside are playgrounds and two exercise fields for young children to play.

Dormitories There are two dormitories, one for boys and one for girls. The boys' dormitory was completed in January 1933 and is divided into two parts, one for junior high school students and one for senior high school students. The first floor of the dormitory houses the living quarters of faculty members with families and a faculty lounge. The first floor of the girls' dormitory is used as a sickroom, a physical examination room, and a clinic.

Dining Hall and Music Room The first floor of this building has a music room, piano rooms, and practice rooms, all separated by solid walls and double glass doors, as well as a student lounge, laundry room, and storage room. The second floor houses the student dining hall, kitchen, and faculty dining hall.

Gymnasium and Covered Playground The gymnasium has a basketball court, male and female shower rooms, locker rooms, and a physical education instructor's office. There is also a covered playground, which was built in September 1933. The covered playground has a novel design, with a wall facing north and ventilation on the other three sides, which is in line with the principles of outdoor activities.

Sports Field The school grounds are spacious, and various sports fields, such as football fields, lacrosse fields, and tennis courts, are fully equipped. Recently, a new quarter-mile-long running track has been completed, which can be considered the best running track in Chinese schools.

Other Buildings The water heater room is located behind the dining hall and provides hot water and heating for the entire school. There are also cloakrooms, toilets, water towers, pumping rooms, bicycle storage rooms, plumber's room, school worker's dormitory, campus guidance office, and gatehouse scattered throughout the school.

Administrative Organization According to the school's regulations, the school's administrative power is concentrated in the hands of the principal, who is responsible for all school affairs. However, according to the school principal's repeated and sincere statements, although he has the power of absolute discretion, he exercises his power in the spirit of democracy. In terms of organization, the principal is assisted in handling school affairs by a registrar, a business manager, division supervisors, and male and female dormitory supervisors. The registrar is similar to the academic affairs director in Chinese schools and is also responsible for smaller disciplinary matters. The business manager is responsible for the cleanliness, procurement, and accommodation of the entire school. The division supervisors assist the principal in supervising teaching. The male and female dormitory supervisors are responsible for guiding the boarders in the male and female dormitories and handling matters that occur in the dormitories. All faculty and staff hold monthly meetings to make decisions. The faculty and staff meeting is not an administrative meeting but a research meeting, where all faculty and staff discuss teaching issues and exchange research ideas. Other committees meet irregularly, and the matters they recommend must be approved by the principal before they can be implemented.

Financial Income and Expenditure The school's budget for this year is 300,000 yuan. In terms of income, tuition and miscellaneous fees for the whole year amount to 250,000 yuan, accounting for five-sixths of the total income. Therefore, the tuition fees paid by the school's students are quite high; the exact amount varies depending on the grade level and whether the student is a day student or a boarder. The remaining 50,000 yuan is freely donated by American community groups and expatriates in Shanghai. The school has 500 students this semester, representing 370 families. Assuming that there are 1,000 students throughout the year, representing 740 families, the average cost of education per student per year is 300 yuan, and the average cost of education borne by each family for their children per year is 400 yuan. However, according to the school principal's report, the actual average cost of education per student per year and the average cost of education borne by each family for their children per year are not as high as these figures, because a portion of the 300,000 yuan in total annual expenditures is board and lodging fees for boarders, which should not be included in the cost of education. In terms of expenditures, in addition to board and lodging fees for boarders, faculty salaries account for 70% of the remaining total expenditures. The remaining operating expenses and equipment costs are all spent according to the budget.

Sports News

Qu Qiu Bo, Xu Chengji, Wins Three Straight Sets Against Carson 165

Six to Three, Six to Three, Six to One. Leaves Shanghai for France on Italian Mail Steamer This Afternoon

Xu Chengji, the representative of our country in this year's Davis Cup tennis team, is scheduled to leave the country on the Italian mail steamer Victoria this afternoon. The Chinese Tennis Club specially invited Xu and Carson to play a singles exhibition match at the club's tennis courts on Singapore Road yesterday afternoon at 2:30 PM. Xu defeated Carson three to one the day after his arrival in Shanghai. It was expected that Xu would win again yesterday. The result was six to three, six to three, and six to one. Xu won three straight sets.

Xu Chengji Six…Three Six…Three Six…One Carson

Both Sides Perform

Because it is not tennis season, they lack practice, so both of them do not seem to be at their best, especially Carson. In the first set, both sides played casually, with very little excitement, and the shots were not as steady as usual. From the beginning of the second set, Xu Chengji gradually got into the swing of things. Xu's wonderful shots began to appear under his racket. Carson also tried his best to follow, but every time he failed to achieve what he wanted. The third set was the most exciting part. Xu's forehand diagonal heavy draw was often effective, and he often used feints to distract Carson, who was overwhelmed. The referee's occasional mistakes yesterday also reduced their interest somewhat.

Match Situation

After the start of the match, Xu Chengji shot smoothly, and Carson struggled hard, with several draws. Carson finally won the first game with eight to six. Xu then pulled back a game, and Carson won the second game again. In the fourth game, Carson suddenly became successful and won with a slide. In the sixth game, it was Xu's turn to serve, and he returned the favor in the same way. After that, the competition between the two sides was very fierce. Xu won two consecutive games, and as a result, won the first set with six to three. In the decisive set, Carson still won the first game first, and Xu tied the score and won the third game with a slide. After each side scored two games, Xu continued to draw and press, and quickly ended the second set with six to three. At the beginning of the third set, Carson was already showing fatigue, while Xu became more and more courageous. The volley and diagonal long shots made Carson run around. Carson only won the second game, and the whole game was controlled by Xu. Xu sailed smoothly and won five consecutive games, winning again with six to one. At this point, Xu had won two consecutive sets. The two sides shook hands and stopped fighting.

Leaving the Country This Afternoon Xu is scheduled to leave Shanghai on the Italian mail steamer Victoria at 11:00 AM this afternoon. The ship is berthed at the China Merchants Third Wharf. Lin Baohua and his wife, who are traveling to France at their own expense, will be traveling with him. Cai Huiquan returned to Hong Kong the day before yesterday to take care of personal matters and will wait for Xu and others to pass through Hong Kong before traveling to France on the same ship. Another Davis Cup player, Zheng Zhaojia, will cross the Atlantic directly from the United States and meet Xu in France.

Fourth Moganshan Mountaineering Race 173

82 Men and Women Participants

Departing in the Morning the Day After Tomorrow, Starting from Yucun at 3 PM

66 in the Men's Group, 16 in the Women's Group, Including Both Chinese and Western Nationalities

In order to promote race walking, the Two-Roads Administration will hold a mountaineering race in the quiet and secluded Mogan Mountain, starting from Yucun and ending at the main entrance of the Mogan Mountain Railway Hotel, a distance of six kilometers. It has been held three times in the past. This year's race is scheduled to leave Shanghai by train in the morning the day after tomorrow (the 28th) and start the race at 3 PM. The awards will be held at the same time in both men's and women's groups. The first, second, and third places in each group will be awarded silver cups, silver medals, and silver badges, respectively. Registration ended yesterday, and the participation was extremely enthusiastic, with 66 men and 16 women, including both Chinese and Western nationalities, which is no less than an international competition. The Road Administration Preparatory Committee's allocation of duties is more thorough than in previous sessions.

According to Shantou news, because the three goods are out of stock, customers want to search for them, causing the production price to suddenly become firm and lively, and the increase is close to 3 yuan. In addition to all the external sales, it is difficult to profit from drawing up in Shanghai, so the shipments to Shanghai will rise again.

Popular Lecture

Zheng Chenggong 194

— He Guang

When we mention Zheng Chenggong, we must first talk about Zheng Zhilong. Because if there wasn't such a shrewd and capable father to train him and cultivate him, Zheng Chenggong probably wouldn't be the Zheng Chenggong we are mentioning now.

Zheng Zhilong was originally a pirate. He was righteous and generous, and eager to help others. Therefore, he was very different from ordinary pirates.

He made friends with many righteous people and robbed ships on the seas around Fujian. Later, his influence gradually grew, and the government troops couldn't do anything about him. The Ming Dynasty also knew that this hero could not be subdued by force. So, they changed to a gentle approach and recruited him, appointing him as the General-in-Chief of Fujian.

Once Zheng Zhilong became the General-in-Chief, he began to improve the maritime security. However, at that time, Taiwan was occupied by the Red Hairs—that is, the Dutch. Chinese pirates ran to them for protection. So, it was impossible to eliminate them. Zheng Zhilong was extremely angry at this situation and immediately mobilized his navy, personally leading the charge. A mighty fleet sailed towards Taiwan to fight the Red Hairs.

When they went into battle, his soldiers all fought with the strength of a hundred men each, bravely advancing forward. However, the Red Hairs' weapons were very powerful: they were all cannons and guns and things like that. The Ming soldiers had never seen anything like this before and were immediately flustered. They trampled on each other, and the formation was in great disarray. The Red Hairs took the opportunity to launch a fierce attack, defeating Zheng Zhilong severely. He had no choice but to flee back to Fujian.

Every time Zheng Zhilong mentioned this crushing defeat, he would grind his teeth and consider it a lifelong regret. He often said to his son, "Chenggong! Remember this defeat and strive to take revenge in the future!"

Although Zheng Chenggong was a child, he understood his father's meaning and vowed to avenge him.

When he grew up, he was indeed braver than his father and also resourceful. So, he led troops to attack Taiwan. No matter how fierce the Red Hairs' cannons were, he was not afraid at all, and he charged forward, leading by example. When the soldiers saw that their commander was risking his life like this, who would dare to retreat? They all charged forward like fierce tigers. Once they got close, the cannons became useless. A fierce melee ensued, and the Red Hairs were utterly defeated and fled in disarray. —These are all Zheng Chenggong's later great achievements. Now let us talk about his patriotic actions at the end of the Ming Dynasty!

During the late Ming Dynasty, the country was in chaos, and bandits rose up everywhere. Li Zicheng marched from Shaanxi to Beijing. Emperor Chongzhen hanged himself on Coal Hill. Wu Sangui, because Li Zicheng's general Liu Zongmin seized his beloved concubine, asked the Qing troops to quell Li Zicheng. But after the rebellion was put down, the Qing troops refused to leave and completely occupied the Ming Dynasty's territory. As a result, all Chinese people became citizens of a conquered nation. But the will of the people did not die, and they rose up one after another to establish the descendants of the Ming Dynasty as emperors: there was Prince Tang in Fujian, Prince Fu in Nanjing, and Prince Lu in Zhejiang. It was most heartbreaking that they could not unite themselves and instead fought for the throne. Therefore, they were completely destroyed by the Manchus using a strategy of divide and conquer.

At that time, Zheng Zhilong was under Prince Tang. After Prince Tang was defeated, he was captured by the Qing troops and imprisoned in Beijing. Zheng Chenggong was greatly saddened by this tragic situation of national subjugation. He vowed to restore the Ming Dynasty.

He gathered many troops and occupied the coastal areas, preparing to build a foundation for a northern expedition.

Zheng Chenggong realized that the many defeats in the past were due to the lack of training and strict discipline of the troops. So, he actively trained the army and navy. Whenever he had time, he would give speeches to the soldiers about the great righteousness of the nation, telling them that the country did not belong to the emperor, but to all the people, and that everyone should take responsibility for saving the country. Therefore, his soldiers all loved the country and the people. In addition, rewards and punishments were clear, and no one under him disobeyed him. He could truly be called having strong soldiers and brave generals.

He called himself the Loyal Earl Grand General of Pacification. He occupied Xiamen, renamed it Siming Prefecture, and the headquarters of the Grand General of Pacification was located here.

At that time, the descendants of the Ming Dynasty occupied Guangxi and were known as Prince Gui. Chenggong further allied with him, and their influence became even greater. Countless heroes from all over the world came to join them, drawn by their reputation. Seeing that his foundation was solid, Zheng Chenggong launched a northern expedition.

At this time, the Qing court had already stabilized the situation and was in the process of rewarding meritorious officials. So, they were completely unprepared. Zheng Chenggong used swift and decisive tactics to march straight from Fujian to Zhejiang, as if entering an uninhabited land. In a few days, he had already reached the territory of Jiangsu. He took Guazhou, broke through Suzhou, and marched straight to Zhenjiang. He was invincible wherever he went.

After these several major battles, Zheng Chenggong knew that the Qing army had a lot of cavalry, and it would be somewhat disadvantageous to fight them with infantry. He then devised a plan: he specially trained a team of soldiers, having them wear iron clothes, hold short knives, lie on the ground, and specialize in cutting the legs of cavalry horses. With this strategy, the Qing soldiers simply couldn't cope and fled at the mere sight of them. Therefore, Zheng Chenggong came to Zhenjiang smoothly.

Zhenjiang was an important town on the south bank of the Yangtze River. Its western side was Nanjing. After occupying Zhenjiang, Zheng Chenggong moved his troops westward and besieged Nanjing. Once Nanjing fell, he could cross the river northward and drive straight in, who could fear he wouldn't be unstoppable?

On this day, Zheng Chenggong was preparing to attack the city when suddenly a messenger-like person came and said to him, "Marshal! We have wanted to surrender to you for a long time, but our families are in Beijing, and we are afraid they will be implicated. If we surrender a month later, it won't matter much. Will the marshal agree to us?" Chenggong was hesitating, and his generals all said, "Nanjing is already like a fish in a pot, is it possible for it to run away? Marshal, agree to them!" Chenggong was originally a magnanimous person, and after hearing these words, he readily agreed. Little did he know that this was their delaying tactic!

In the blink of an eye, a month had passed. On the 29th, Zheng Chenggong distributed lamb and fine wine and generously rewarded his soldiers, preparing to enter the city the next day.

In the evening, the soldiers were all drunk and returned to camp to rest. Who knew that disaster would strike at this time?

It turned out that reinforcements had arrived and had already made arrangements with those inside the city to attack from both sides. When the Zheng army woke up from their dreams in shock, how could they have the ability to resist? They scattered and fled, looking like a complete mess.

Zheng Chenggong was heartbroken. The plans he had worked so hard on for several years were ruined in an instant due to a moment of carelessness. When would such achievements be able to be restored? How could he not be heartbroken and sad?

But he was, after all, a person of strong will and was not discouraged at all. After retreating to Xiamen, he reorganized the remnants of his army: eliminating the old and weak and replenishing them with strong men. He crossed the Taiwan Strait to Taiwan, drove away the Red Hairs, and occupied Taiwan. Firstly, to make it an overseas base, and secondly, to avenge his father's defeat and fulfill his long-cherished wish. —As for his battle against the Red Hairs, it has already been mentioned earlier, so there is no need to mention it again here.

After Zheng Chenggong occupied Taiwan, he revitalized industry, developed mineral resources, and founded education. In a few years, he had governed it into a place of strong soldiers and wealthy people. However, his heart for restoring the Ming Dynasty never faded. However, at that time, the Manchus' power became increasingly prosperous, and in addition, the generals under him secretly surrendered to the Manchus. Therefore, Chenggong not only could not attack the Qing Dynasty, but would instead be attacked by the Qing Dynasty. Even so, Chenggong built strong fortifications, and the Qing troops could only sigh in vain!

Zheng Chenggong still used the Ming Dynasty's reign title. Unfortunately, he soon passed away! Later, it was passed down to his grandson Zheng Keshuang before being destroyed by the Manchus. At this time, it had been more than thirty years since the fall of the Ming Dynasty.

Louis Pasteur (1822-1895) 195

— Zheng Kan

In the early 19th century, there was a middle-aged leather craftsman in France who often hid alone in the dark and sighed. One day, a charitable old man noticed him. The old man saw that he was poorly dressed and assumed that he must be worried about poverty, so he intended to help him and sincerely asked him, "Friend, please forgive my intrusion, what difficulties do you have? Can I help you?" When he heard the old man's words, he quickly stood up and bowed respectfully to the old man. His face was red, and he couldn't speak for a long time. The old man saw that he was an honest man and assumed that he must have an unspeakable secret, so he felt even more pity for him and said, "Friend, just tell me the amount you need." He knew that the old man had misunderstood him, so he had to tell the real reason and said, "Sir, thank you! Although I am poor, I don't want money. I hate that I am old and uneducated, and too useless! I am troubled here because I want to find an opportunity to study, but I can't find it." When the old man saw that he was so eager to learn, he was very respectful and promised to teach him himself. He took the old man as his teacher and never sighed again. He got up before dawn to make leather and finished his work early to go to the old man's house to study. He often studied until late at night and was reluctant to come back. He often forgot to eat dinner. Because he worked so hard, he naturally made progress very quickly. In less than a year, he could study on his own without a teacher.

At that time, he lived in Arblis and was already the father of four children. His wages were very low, and a family of six lived a very hard life. The workers in the same situation as him sent their children to the factory as child laborers. Some people advised him to do the same, but he declined, saying, "I believe I am a useful person, but unfortunately I am uneducated and have wasted my life. How can I bear to waste my children's lives? I would rather eat one meal and starve one meal than let them go to school." He really ate one meal and starved one meal, saving money to send his children to school to pay tuition. He also took the time out of his busy schedule to teach them the words he knew. Because of his hard work, he ended up making his fourth son, Louis Pasteur, into one of the greatest scientists of the 19th century. Most other scientists can only provide convenience to mankind, but his invention saved the lives of all mankind.

Pasteur was a very ambitious child. He saw that his father worked so hard to send him to school and was very grateful. He vowed to become a great man to repay his father. Therefore, he studied especially hard. He was a famous good student at school. In 1843, Pasteur was already 21 years old. One day, he said to his father, "Dad, you have worked hard for decades. Your son is now grown up and should share some of your burden. He shouldn't just let Dad work and his son study." Soon, he was admitted to the Paris Normal School, where he worked part-time and studied part-time. His father was afraid that he would overwork himself and often wrote to advise him, "Son, great talents are often late bloomers. Don't be anxious. Working too hard will harm your body. You must get enough sleep every day and don't forget to exercise. Because only with a healthy body can you do great things."

Pasteur listened to his father and paid attention to his health and self-cultivation. He knew that competing with others for scores in the examination hall was harmful and useless. He didn't care about this and concentrated on doing scientific experiments in the laboratory. He was very patient and meticulous, using a long time to gradually prove the truth through trial experiments. Many students who were eager for quick success and superficial understanding laughed at him for being useless and gave him the nickname "the pillar of the laboratory." Only his friend Chappuis understood him. Chappuis often said to those who ridiculed Pasteur, "You are blind. You will know what kind of person Pasteur is in the future."

Pasteur didn't care whether people praised him or scolded him, he only knew how to work hard. He liked to study crystallography very much and gradually experimented with the truth. In 1848, the Minister of Public Education recommended him to Strasburg as a professor of chemistry. There he met a lady who loved science, and they got married that year. After the wedding, he asked his wife, "Love, where should we go on our honeymoon?" His wife replied sincerely, "What place is more suitable than the laboratory!" She gently kissed Pasteur's forehead, with a few points of shyness in her eyes, and said in a low voice, "Love, I love to see you working in the laboratory." She closed her eyes, recalling and continuing, "Your face is full of enthusiasm, your eyes are shining, you are seriously facing the crystal in front of you, whether it is a meticulous experiment or a deep consideration, I can see the joy in the depths of your heart... and there is more, but it may not be possible to describe in words. Love, in short, you are in a laboratory, like a fish in a deep pool, both happy and beautiful!"

Pasteur was encouraged by his wife and worked harder, spending all his honeymoon time in the laboratory. Now his work was making amazing progress day by day, and he couldn't let go of it more and more, so he simply experimented day and night. Sometimes he came back too late and saw his wife waiting for him with a candle, he felt a little sorry and smiled to comfort her, "Love, I will soon have an unprecedented great invention. Please be patient for a while, I will soon be able to make you famous." Sure enough, soon after, because of his successful research on winemaking, the French government awarded him the honorable Legion of Honor, and also appointed him as professor and dean of the Lille Science Society.

At that time, the whole world believed that "things must rot first, and then insects are born," and no one knew how to prevent external microorganisms. Therefore, germs bred everywhere, and I don't know how many people died in vain. Even contemporary scientists, the director of the Rouen Museum, Pouchet, also believed that microorganisms are transformed from dead matter into living ones, and are naturally generated in artificial air and oxygen. However, Pasteur had already seen that this "theory of spontaneous generation" was wrong when he studied yeast. He advocated that "things must first have insects (i.e., microorganisms), and then rot." He believed that there must be many microorganisms in the air that cause substances to rot. So he worked hard to do an experiment to overthrow this "theory of spontaneous generation."

During his vacation, when he had time, he took dozens of bottles, each containing a substance that was easy to rot. He put them in groups in different regions. After a few days, he took the bottles back. He found that of the 20 bottles placed on the mountain road near his hometown, 8 had rotted; of the 20 bottles placed on the mountain, 5 had rotted; of the 20 bottles placed on the ice sea, only 1 had rotted; of the 20 bottles placed in a crowded lecture hall, all had rotted. Later, he did another experiment. He took two bottles containing easily rotten liquids, used high heat to kill the microorganisms in the liquids and bottles, and then opened the bottle mouths to let air into the bottles. As a result, the next day, the liquid in one bottle rotted, and the liquid in one bottle was as fresh as ever. It turned out that in the bottle that did not rot, before it was heated, Pasteur devised a way to bend the bottleneck so that air could enter the bottle, but the microorganisms stopped at the bottleneck. Without microorganisms causing trouble, the liquid inside did not spoil. He repeated the experiment again and again, and it always worked. Everyone then believed that what made substances rot was indeed a microorganism—bacteria; if it was isolated, the substance would not rot.

He used his new invention to prove that germs can invade the living tissue of the human body, so surgery must be absolutely clean, and the equipment used must also be disinfected. Based on his principles, he also invented vaccination. After Pasteur's germ theory became popular, Western medicine made great progress, and the number of people who died in vain in the world was greatly reduced.

At that time, French industry was declining sharply, but suddenly it was revived, all thanks to Pasteur's invention of winemaking and silkworm disease prevention methods. Huxley said, "The income from one invention of Pasteur is enough to compensate for the indemnity of the Franco-Prussian War of 1871 by more than 5,000 trillion francs."

Pasteur's father lived to a ripe old age. He saw his son's great inventions succeed one by one with his own eyes. Usually, when his son was doing experiments, he also learned from his son. Therefore, his knowledge also increased with age. In his old age, he could not only understand his son's knowledge, but he himself became a scholar.

Publishing Industry

The Publishing Industry and the Literacy Movement 196

— Ze Fu

The call for "universal education" has been around for decades, but until now, the lack of universal education in China remains the same. Precisely because universal education is advocated but education is still not universal, some overly clever people have begun to suspect that Chinese characters are too difficult. Thus, the promotion of simplified characters began, followed by the promotion of Romanization. On the surface, those who advocate simplified characters or Romanization may have some reasons, and some current periodicals have already applied these simplified characters. However, as an author, I am ashamed to say that I cannot recognize a few simplified characters. On the contrary, I encountered considerable obstacles when reading. Therefore, I often have the following feelings: People who have received higher education are certainly not confused. They only need to read the simplified character table several times to remember it. However, knowing two ways of writing a character is not without a sense of "busybodying." For people who are just learning to read, many problems will arise. First, if you only read simplified characters, then even a simplified character dictionary is not available. Isn't it as difficult as climbing to heaven to look up a character? Second, if people who are roughly literate want to read more kinds of books and newspapers, it is definitely not enough to only know simplified characters. Then they still have to understand the original font. Third, the structure of Chinese characters originally has its own certain rules, and those who have dabbled in the field of philology are very familiar with it. Simplified characters are not like that. They are the vulgar writing of business circles in various places. Because the font structure is chaotic and there is no certain standard, it is difficult for scholars to remember. Therefore, the promotion of simplified characters may seem to be conducive to universal education on the surface, but in reality, it adds another layer of difficulty. As for the Romanization of Chinese characters, there is no need to say more. You must know that China's ability to nurture within the same cultural sphere, despite its vast territory, large population, and complex languages, relies on the unification of this writing system. Now, advocating Romanization means first destroying all the hard work of the past thousands of years in the field of writing. And relying solely on the phonetic Latin script to make all Chinese people able to write and understand it, isn't this a dream? For example, a Latin script spelled by a Suzhou person cannot be understood by a Changzhou person, let alone a Hangzhou or Nanjing person. This is not so much helping China's universal education as it is an attempt to destroy Chinese culture. Therefore, the author believes that the reason why education in China has not been popularized is not because there is a problem with the writing tool, but because the work of promoting universal education has not been vigorously advanced. No matter how simple and easy something is, if you don't put in a little effort and hope to succeed without any effort, there is absolutely no such legendary truth in the world. The same is true for the anti-illiteracy movement. The slogan of "universal education" has been shouted for decades, but it is only shouted, not done. As a result, despite decades of complaining in magazines, newspapers, and publications, China's illiteracy will not be eliminated by one person. Since last year, the Shanghai Municipal Literacy Movement Committee launched the literacy movement, and after only half a year, although there is no formal work report, according to internal staff of the committee, about 120,000 illiterate people have been eliminated. This proves that the work of universal education is not in saying but in doing. Promoting this work will always have a way, always have an effect, and always have hope. Not promoting this work, but stealing and tricking to advocate simplified characters and Romanization, then the work of universal education will always be hopeful.

Since we understand that the key to this literacy movement is not in talking but in doing, it is not enough for only those responsible for the literacy movement to do it. You must know that after reading for two or three months and knowing one or two thousand characters, you may be unexpectedly successful and achieve remarkable results when you are learning, but once you leave school, after half a year or a year, you may still forget everything and become illiterate again. Why? Because there are too few opportunities to apply it. It is not enough to read general newspapers and periodicals. It is absolutely impossible to rely solely on the opportunity to write letters or write accounts. If you always read this literacy textbook, you will never review the old and know the new. Some people may say that children's reading materials can be given to people who are just learning to read. In fact, it is also impossible because the content of children's reading materials is often created in accordance with the psychology and physiology of children. A story for children to read will definitely not be of interest to adults. Therefore, the author believes that in today's world where the government authorities are working hard to promote the literacy movement, the publishing industry should do its best to assist. How to assist? Taking Shanghai as an example, it is to provide 120,000 newly eliminated illiterate people with suitable and good reading materials, publish a periodical, or publish a set of common sense books. In short, taking these newly eliminated illiterate adults as the target, using the one or two thousand characters they know, work hard to compile various essays, stories, novels, etc. If it is a periodical, then of course you can insert many current affairs materials. This kind of publication has two advantages: illiterate people who are studying can use it as extracurricular and supplementary reading materials, and graduates can increase their reading opportunities and avoid wasting their studies.

If the publishing industry can lower its pricing and improve its content, then on the one hand, it can assist this literacy movement, so that it can achieve more practical results, and at the same time, it can obtain a wide range of readers. The author firmly believes that if only 120,000 illiterate people have been eliminated in a corner of Shanghai, there can be at least 12,000 copies of sales. If we cooperate with the Shanghai Municipal Literacy Movement Committee, then through the publicity of the principals and teachers of the literacy schools, the extent of its sales will be far more than tens of thousands of copies.

The Publishing Industry and the Reading Community 197

— Zhuang Xin Zai

It's time for a rectification movement

To say that the Chinese publishing industry is an exaggeration. In reality, China only has book selling.

The publishing industry is indeed aimed at the reading community, but the publishing industry cannot be like the Parisian perfume market, purely catering to general modern tastes.

The so-called problem with the Chinese publishing industry is that the reading community does not improve due to the inducement of the publishing industry. On the contrary, the publishing industry falls by catering to the tastes of the reading community.

What kind of embrace does the Chinese publishing industry have for readers? In order to grasp the general low-level tastes of readers, absurd and obscene novels and notes such as "The Strange Adventures of ××" and "The Karma of ××" are filling the Chinese publishing market. And 70% to 80% of periodicals use comics, witty sketches, and short essays as the backbone. Looking back at the contribution of the publishing industry to the reading community, it is naturally taking the revamped and largely similar textbooks of various levels as the center of profit. In addition, piecing together and reprinting some kind of series, some kind of complete works, some kind of selected works, and so on, after messing around, they are still these old things with new wine in old bottles. The May Fourth Movement introduced some basic knowledge of science and brought some modern superficialities. The New Literature Movement, without selection, chaotically published some colorful poems and novels. Following that was the social science movement, which contributed the undigested and half-understood ABCs of Marxism and books such as the Outline of Social Science. This is still an exaggeration in terms of the bright side. As for competing to compile test question answer keys and scrambling to reprint ancient books with several discounts, the former guides young students to cheating and opportunistic methods, making them unwilling to put in hard work for in-depth research in academic research, and the latter's selection is inclined towards low-level tastes. The poor printing and many errors in proofreading are not worth mentioning. (To be continued)

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

Europe's Bargaining Politics 198

— Yang

The new peace plan signed by the four countries of England, France, Belgium, and Italy was announced simultaneously in London and Paris on the 20th. It consists of nine articles, the most important of which are: "Condemnation of Germany's unilateral abolition of international obligations; The Locarno Treaty remains effective; The area within 20 kilometers east of the border between France and Belgium will be guarded by international troops." In presenting this new plan, the four countries also clearly knew that Germany would not accept these conditions. However, they first opened a price to see how Germany would counteroffer.

Although Germany's reply has not yet arrived, based on what Hitler has expressed and the domestic opinions in the past two days, it is clear that it is far from the issue. The German chief representative, Ribbentrop, told British Foreign Secretary Eden that "Germany cannot accept any proposals to resolve the Rhine problem if it cannot enjoy equal treatment." Hitler said in a speech in Jena that "the German nation is now seeking complete autonomy. We will never give way to any concept that attempts to threaten us. The Treaty of Versailles is like a tombstone, only enough for mourning and not enough to be the cornerstone of a new world order." An important figure in the German Ministry of Foreign Affairs said more ridiculously on the 21st, "This document is based on the spirit of the Treaty of Versailles. When politicians gathered in London yesterday, they almost got the date wrong, thinking they were still 17 years ago." According to the above statements from various important German figures, Germany may not be willing to counteroffer at such a price. Even if they do counteroffer, it must be a high price and a low payment, without any doubt.

Does this mean that this deal will definitely fail? No. Britain knew early on that Germany would not accept such conditions. Therefore, British Prime Minister Eden said again yesterday that "everything in the Locarno plan is just a suggestion from the four countries. If Germany proposes another plan to maintain the overall situation during the interim period before a new solution is reached and can gain the agreement of the four countries, it may be changed." The meaning is, our asking price is like this, if you want to counteroffer, as long as we can make back our costs, we can sell at a loss to attract more business. Also, on the 21st, London newspapers unanimously revealed news of opposition to the draft four-power agreement in the British House of Commons, allowing the temporary stationing of international troops on the German border. The regulations on the military and political obligations borne by Britain. From this point of view, the so-called new plan established by the four countries will not only be unacceptable to Germany, but it is not even consistent within itself. How can it achieve any effect? I did not expect that the so-called high-minded European diplomats would be so reckless, not only failing to see the momentum of Germany, but also failing to see the world situation. Japan's invasion of China and Italy's attack on Abyssinia, although there was a time when the international community made righteous speeches, soon disappeared without a trace, and there was no way to correct them. Now, Germany is demanding equal treatment and reclaiming its own sovereignty, but they want to desperately contain it, which is not only clearly unfair, but also contrary to reason. Moreover, sanctions against Germany are neither easy nor possible. It can be seen that the methods of European diplomats are just so-so. Therefore, for the sake of the four countries, the only thing to do is to ignore the established facts and the broken treaties, and re-establish a new collective security plan, which is necessary.

Disturbance 199

— Xu Ji

Early in the morning, the sun shone high on the wall, displaying a solemn and tranquil atmosphere amidst the hustle and bustle. As a result, the small alley began to liven up; this small alley, in its outward simplicity, perfectly reflected the status of the more than twenty households living in it: shop assistants, rickshaw pullers, small clerks, clandestine workers... all those who were forgotten by the world, abandoned by the golden laughter of the metropolis, crowded, jumbled, in this dirty and simple housing without sunbathing lawns and dance halls, living day after day in these days of suffering and anxiety...

The small alley in the early morning was lively: men successively rushed on the road to labor in the busy life. As a result, women gathered by the public tap, washing some vegetables, washing some clothes, talking about other people's and their own trivial matters, venting some resentment and sorrow about life: cursing, sighing...

Children cried and ran all over the alley, and the adults frowned: "That kind of life, that kind of days!"

So, someone pointed to the third back door, as if revealing a treasure, and said to an old woman washing rice beside her: "Look, at A'Mao's house, the man has lost his job, and he wants to die all day long. He cried all night again yesterday! The couple cried together, making us unable to sleep well all night, really... alas, really..."

"In this day and age, living is not a joke. If it is—"

Suddenly, the back door of the "A'Mao" house that had been pointed at was suddenly opened as if it had been hit by a storm, and a sharp, anxious cry shot out like an arrow, pulling all the people's eyes over; people stared blankly at the low door frame with a curious and sighing mood. All the sounds were also temporarily quiet, and in the silence, someone said in a low voice: "Look, this kind of life, this kind of..."

The sharp cry still pierced straight into everyone's ears and hearts. Then, like a madman, the young wife of "A'Mao" suddenly rushed out of the house, crashing like a mad beast, and even the tone of crying became a terrible roar.

The women went to hold her, surrounded her, and some people listened with great interest, like reading an interesting picture story.

"A'Mao... he swallowed opium and died! These days... how am I... going to live... die! Die! God... God..."

"What? A'Mao is dead?" The voice was surprise and terror.

"You have to report it. It's suicide, not a joke."

The voices suddenly became chaotic again, and many people walked into the low door to climb up to the dark loft to see. The dead person lay on the bunk, with a terrible dark face: "So pitiful, still a young person, these days..."

Others were arranging for the young A'Mao's wife: comforting her, or donating a little scarce money...

So, someone went to report to the bureau. The bureau came with a corpse cart and policemen, and quickly carried the corpse away, and called the living person to ask some questions. "The past is the past", everything is over...

At noon, people began to cook again, all the disturbances had calmed down, and this small disturbance had completely passed. The small alley was deathly silent, restoring its original appearance. Only some dark and sad shadows remained, unconsciously appearing and disappearing in some people's hearts.

"Life is so terrible."

However, in fact, just like all ordinary things, after a few days, this small disturbance that had already passed was gradually forgotten...

Page 18

A Heartbreaking Story 200

— Bai Ling

That was a long, long time ago, when I was still in Qingdao. Once, I was sent by a women's group to a small village in Sifang, not far from the island, to do some work. Accidentally rushing out of the city, my nostrils, which had been suffocated by coal smoke, immediately felt a new sensation: the spring fields sent me a fragrant smell of yellow soil.

I walked forward along a small path covered with green grass. At that time, there was really a kind of heartwarming taste that made me laugh uncontrollably. Although it was not far from the city, everything reflected in my eyes was already something from another world. I walked into a small village, and my eyes were filled with some lovely and simple people. Because I wanted to know their living conditions, I did not ask for anyone's permission, so I rushed into a dilapidated small family in a busy and lively manner. The door was so low that I had to bend down to enter. This family was just eating lunch, which was: sweet potato dried porridge, and sorghum noodles made into steamed buns. They asked me to sit down in a friendly manner, so I sat down happily at the table where they were eating. The woman in the family looked like a widow, and there was no man in the house, only five boys and girls of different ages. Among them were three older girls, who were so thin that they didn't look like human beings at all. I once asked the oldest one, who was fifteen or sixteen years old, "What do your sisters do at home"?

She said in a low voice: "No. We all work in factories".

Her words made it unnecessary for me to ask any further questions, so:

"Are you all in one factory?"

"No, I'm in the Dakang Yarn Factory, which is opened by the Japanese. My two sisters are in the British Tobacco Company."

"What do you all do?" I asked again.

"There's no good work to do in the factory! Isn't it just suffering to the extreme! I'm in the spinning room. They are in..." Just as she wanted to continue, her two sisters interrupted and interjected in unison: "We shred tobacco for others".

After talking about some other things, I asked her again: "Is your foreman female or male? Is he strict?

She pouted and said: "He is a terrible male guy. That thing always bullies us female workers. He likes to drink alcohol. Once he gets drunk, he loses his temper, or he goes to the pretty female workers to say bad things! We've really had enough of it! Alas, what can we do."

"How much do you get paid every day?"

She smiled, showing hesitation, and said: "It's not the same. Um, it's too little. I only get two dimes a day after counting."

At this time, a woman's urgent call came from the family next door: "Sister Chunmei, have you finished eating? Let's go."

This one who was called Chunmei was the girl who was talking to me. After being called, she quickly stood up, wiped the corners of her mouth with her hand, and said to me with a smile: "I'm really sorry, we're still waiting to go to work, I can't talk to you anymore.

As she walked out of the gate courteously, I asked the two little girls sitting next to me, "What about you two"?

The two girls looked at me with gloomy eyes, and then looked at her, but they didn't say a word to me after all. At this time, her mother opened a sad mouth and said slightly: "Alas, neither of them has a job. One was sick for half a month and just got out of bed. One was rejected by the foreman's inspection, saying that she was too young and couldn't do anything.

My heart fell heavily into a shadow.

The woman said again: "That's why the older girl can bring money home every day to support us. We also rely on her. These short-lived ghosts, their father died early..."

Suddenly, a woman around thirty years old ran in from outside the gate. She opened her mouth wide and laughed loudly: "Chunmei's mother, you don't have to call Chunmei to work anymore. Don't you know that Wang Gui's Liu Jie in the west is crying at home. She just ran back from the factory. She said that she didn't get a job today and was tricked by a foreman to go to the mountain. Um, um, the child's clothes were also torn! It is said that she was beaten by the foreman in the end, and she vomited blood from her mouth..."

This wildfire-like news burned my heart.

However, within a few minutes, this small village was immersed in miserable crying. Oh, Wang Gui's daughter, who had been ravaged by the foreman, finally sacrificed in the hands of violent forces.

Nonsense 201

— (Blow)

The four countries of England, France, Belgium, and Italy signed a new peace plan. The full text of the agreement was announced simultaneously in London and Paris. The general idea of ​​the new peace plan is not to pursue the established facts of Germany, but to prevent future wars. Tan Lao San said, "It is not too late to mend the fold after the sheep are lost," but after all, the sheep have already been lost, but it is indeed better than not being able to mend the fold after the sheep are lost.

The British Foreign Secretary declared that he would strive to rebuild European peace, stating roughly that the infantry squads of the Locarno Public Kingdom, formed into an international army, should be stationed on the borders of France, Germany, and Belgium. During the negotiation period, Germany should be responsible for not increasing the garrison in the Rhine. Tan Lao San said that the German army has already been stationed in the Rhine region. How can it be withdrawn and allow international troops to be stationed? Germany has stationed troops in the Rhine. So how can the increase or decrease of troops be limited? Foreigners like to sign blank checks, mostly like this.

The Blind Singer 202

— Xin Ye

On that long sandy road, he used that thin bamboo cane every day, knocking on each sandy strip, step by step, along the wall of Zhang's courtyard. Although his eyes were blind, he was very familiar with this road; not only familiar, he remembered very clearly which sandy strips were laid on this road, which ones were broken, and that there was a small bridge at the end of Zhang's courtyard.

In the summer, the scorching sun hung in the sky like fire, shining beads of sweat on his forehead, and a stench permeated his dirty and tattered shirt and trousers. But he still passed through that long sandy road every day as usual, walking into every village and every alley -

In winter, the northwest wind blew, and snowflakes fluttered. Although he only wore a thin, tattered cotton-padded jacket given to him by others, and his body trembled in the northwest wind like a vibrating string, he still passed through this long sandy road every day, walking into every village and every alley.

He was a lonely, blind singer. There was no joy or comfort around him, and he never thought of so-called happiness in life. He was like a lonely statue in a dilapidated temple, spending desolate and tragic years; every day, he had to sing for a living.

Every time, when he passed the Mei Hua Bridge and the thin bamboo cane knocked into the Bai Sui Alley, making some strange echoes, he would lengthen that slightly melancholic and trembling tune and sing:

Life is a dream, a gray and short dream;

In this dreamland, I have not seen a ray of light.

I do not believe that there is any happiness and joy in the world,

I only know to strive for a little superficial rights and fame!

Because I no longer want to see the world's filth and humanity's ugliness,

So I am willing to be a blind singer;

I want to shout open the secrets of the universe, I want to shout out the dumb riddle of life,

But oh, spring goes and autumn comes year after year,

The long sky is vast, the earth is vast,

Forever, forever, the universe is still silent...

Singing, singing, he did not hope that more people could understand what this song was saying, but he just wanted to pour out some sorrow into this vast and boundless universe.

High-rise Building 203

— Xiao Wen

"Street scenes" are not as simple as the coming and going of vehicles and horses.

Since I moved into the high-rise building, it was certainly an accidental thing. Looking down from the window, there is a busy street in front, and all kinds of things are taken into view. This is not enjoyment. People who live in high-rise buildings are not necessarily the masters of material things. Seeing the pedestrians outside stride forward, I feel that my soul is like a caged bird, even if there is good food in the cage, and the cage bars are dazzling gold. I no longer hope to live in a high-rise building. Isn't a prison also a tall building? Although it is high, it cannot climb to heaven. Wouldn't living in a low house go to hell?

When I idly look at the street, it is considered a leisure pastime, stealing a bit of strength from the heavy burden. Every time I think silently, the backs of the pedestrians passing by, regardless of age, a child, a bearded man, all feel the same sadness to me. It's not theirs, it should be my own sorrow.

In the morning, the street is very quiet. Those who get up early include workers, students, and vendors - some people with the same fate, strangely energetic. Whether it is spring or winter, the spirit of heroism is not necessarily their own. Perhaps it is because the whip of life is drawn on their backs, like horses and donkeys blindly walking a road that cannot be finished, forward! Forward! Who can say for sure that it is a "broad road"? The attitude of the students carrying their schoolbags is sincere. The rickshaw pullers carry the handles of their cars, dragging empty cars, without customers wandering, which is a leisure annoyance. The newspaper sellers shout hoarsely like injured people howling. All of this is deeply imprinted in my eyes, a picture of labor, hard work, and the selling of sweat and blood.

Every busy street has a social history. From morning to night, from spring to winter, it shows the progress of the "fashion" of the young ladies and the popular "handsome" of the young masters. Both women and men, the pretty and the stupid, the heartbroken and the frustrated, and the stories from "birth" to "funeral" are all revealed here. Standing at the window, I not only read a history book, but there are also a lot of lessons in the history book.

Bright Moon Ascends to the East

Quiet, at night, the stars and moon are unusually bright. A corner of a pier in a port town, iron chains and wooden stakes lying there, and large wooden barrels along the edge squatting there like tired cows. Two policemen and a patrol leader walk over.

They are pasting notices along the way, offering a reward of one hundred pounds for the arrest of an escaped convict. This is a key point for escape, and therefore a good place to post notices.

The police opened the paper bag, took out the notice, and asked their patrol leader for instructions; the patrol leader hesitated slightly for a moment: "Okay, post one!" On that wooden barrel that looked like a tired ox squatting there, a "…hair black, eyes black. Height five feet five inches…" bounty notice was posted.

The three people had joy in their hearts, no, maybe they had pain. Although they understood that the escaped convict was a genius, sometimes they hated why they didn't have the opportunity to see him - that escaped convict! But their duty held him tightly.

So, one of the three went to other places to post their notices.

Quiet, with only the patrol leader remaining, he paced back and forth, the light of the stars and moon brought his gaze to the notice that was not yet pasted tightly: "One hundred pounds, and a promotion…" the temptation fluttered before his eyes. He consciously thought of "Many honest people have not seen such a large sum of money!"…

A dark shadow moved from the left, and he knew to shout at him to stop. It was a ragged beggar, a vagrant. While telling the patrol leader that he was a poor song seller, he kept walking forward.

Isn't that right? The poor can be bullied by anyone. He was stopped by the patrol leader's order.

However, he was very witty, he played dumb, he did not get the patrol leader's permission. He sang…

"Life flows like a muddy river,

Machines eat our flesh!

Coal smoke blackens our faces,

Liquor scorches our hearts.

…" Song.

Naturally, that one didn't want to listen anymore and told him to shut up.

He - the vagrant temporarily stopped singing, but became a preacher, and talked and talked to that one. When the patrol leader felt that he himself was also a weak person, being ordered to do dangerous errands, even disregarding having a "family", he couldn't help but feel a resonance of sympathy in his heart for this vagrant in front of him. He continued to sing,…

But this song is a code.

When the two policemen who posted the notices returned, the patrol leader let the vagrant hide without hesitation. He told the two policemen to go first.…

"Goodbye! Friend, thank you. You have been kind to me tonight, I am grateful to you. When we raise the weak and overthrow the strong in the future, I may repay you in the same way… Our positions will all change in the future, until the bright moon rises in the east…" The vagrant walked out of the wooden barrel, waved his hand to the patrol leader, walked down the stairs, and followed the code. - escaped from the one hundred pound reward.

The patrol leader loudly read the "one hundred pounds, one hundred pounds" confession, like being struck by thunder, doubting "Am I really as stupid as I thought I was?"

Guess! That is the escaped convict wanted with a one hundred pound reward!

(Note! "Bright Moon Ascends to the East" is written by Mrs. "Gran Gran" of Ireland. The purpose of the play is to describe the Irish independent revolutionary movement. The dialogue is very serious. I hope the audience will pay attention.) Xing Junming "Falling Sunset Lonely Wild Duck"

Bolt from the blue creates right and wrong

Storytelling 206

Cai Xiaofang's Mao Family Story

Sino-Western (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening: "Jia Baoyu"

Nuwa refines stones to mend the sky. One dull and useless stone was left behind. It endured countless wind, frost, cold, and heat calamities. At the foot of the Great Barren Mountain, it emitted light. Vast and boundless, the Immortal pointed the way. A Mysterious Real Person carried it back. The stubborn stone became spiritually enlightened and entered a mother's womb. It was born into the Jia family's noble lineage. The bestowed childhood name Baoyu was not without meaning. Because, at birth, he came out of the womb holding jade. Lady Dowager Jia cherished him like a treasure. Often worrying about heavy rain and strong winds. His comings and goings were taught by female servants. Then came the exceptionally beautiful Lin Daiyu. She was the first among the Twelve Beauties. They were childhood sweethearts with mutual affection. They spent their days together intimately. Picking flowers and touching grass for joy. Playing with powder and rouge by her eyebrows. Accompanying her in meditation in the embroidered pavilion. What a romantic and suave young master Jia. Speaking of studying, he would frown. Alas, strict family rules forced him to pursue his studies. Xiren and Sheyue often persuaded him, saying, "Stepping on the golden鳌 will bring thunder in spring on flat ground." To obtain the glory of bringing honor to ancestors and revitalizing the family. But he disdained many scholars, saying. Falling leaves and seeds are not for me. Ever since I dreamt of entering the Red Chamber. I have let the ambitions of wealth and fame turn to ashes. Only Miss Lin knows my heart. I willingly die and become flying ashes. Better than monopolizing the鳌's head and enjoying the spring breeze. After enjoying a few years of a young master's fortune. He repaid the effort and reluctantly went to the autumn exam. The water flows eastward and never returns.

Movie News

Silver Jottings 208

— Zhi Er

The screening of "The Story of Louis Pasteur", starring Paul Muni, took place at 11 a.m. yesterday at the Grand Theater (another screening will be held at the Cathay Theater on the 29th at 11 a.m.). "It seems pretty good."

Confucius said: Mr. Shao Zuiweng should see it once, because this is an educational film.

Someone once said that I would be going to "Northern Shanxi" "soon". Not long after, another newspaper specializing in wholesale and retail "Red Stickers" said that "because the Communist bandits suffered a crushing defeat, he decided to stay in Shanghai temporarily".

This trap is really very clever. Knowing that I am "staying in Shanghai", they arranged this set-up. Isn't it "proof" enough in every way?

However, I am silent. Because people have gone to so much trouble to put on this "act", if I were to make a statement again, that would be too "shameless".

A friend once advised me that someone was going to pay a few gangsters ten dollars to "teach" me a lesson. Later, I met Brother Ye Cha, who declared that there was absolutely no such thing. If there is absolutely no such thing, I will avoid a "lesson", which is naturally even better.

Recently, I read Mr. Wu Cun's "self-criticism" and saw the words "old man" in it again, so I couldn't help but think of my friend's words again.

"Teach" me a lesson, okay, let me be "taught" a lesson. As for "jottings", I will still continue to write. Although this seems to make the term "old man" even more applicable.

Roque's "Cowardly Hero" 209

Some people advise the editor, and some people offer suggestions to the editor. In short: they all don't want the jottings to be so "miscellaneous" anymore (the charge is probably that it's too damaging to the dignity of prominent figures, right?)

Advice and suggestions were not enough, so they went a step further and came up with a clever plan while drinking tea at Xinya: calling the advertising department in the name of the ×× Film Company.

Who is the designer, who is the "practitioner", everyone knows in their hearts. "To avoid expanding the dispute and the trouble of correction, I will not discuss it." In short, although this clever plan took a lot of effort, it was not necessarily "brilliant." First, Tianyi Company had used such a clever plan before, this is an old trick. Second, this is still done under a false name, which is inevitably a bit evasive. Third... going on would give the impression of "practicing the art of climbing the dragon". Better not to say it.

Confucius said: "Brilliant"? "Brilliant"?

Confucius said: Mr. Anonymous, after seeing yesterday's Silver Jottings, reportedly went to Mr. Lin at the Datong Apartment on Beile Road without eating breakfast, asking Mr. Lin why he had taken down such a rotten, dirty thing. Mr. Anonymous should know better than anyone who took it down. Thanks to Brother Cunren's introduction, we seemed to nod to each other when we met, even if we weren't quite "friends" yet, it didn't seem necessary to use such not-so-"brilliant" means. If you have any new "gimmicks", please give me a call, and I will definitely go to Xinya to listen to your advice.

"National Beauty" Shatters Dreams 210

People in the inland areas still hold illusions, thinking that Shanghai is paved with gold and everyone rushes to Shanghai to make a living. Little do they know that the Shanghai market is deteriorating every day, and it is more difficult than ascending to heaven to find even a half-time job, resulting in wandering around the city, suffering unspeakable hardships. The "National Beauty" sound film by Shanghai Company, starring Yuan Erchun and Bai Hong, exposes the various economic downturns and difficulties of life in Shanghai to the fullest extent, enough to shatter the dreams of people in the inland areas. The film is released today at the Carlton Theater.
